President Wang's Report

Diplomatic Policy 30

And the Process of Reforming "Official Document Processing"

Diplomatic Policy Consistent with Domestic Policy

(Nanjing) At the Administrative Yuan's weekly memorial meeting on the 28th, attended by over 200 people including ministers and officials of all departments, President Wang presided and reported on the issue of diplomatic policy and the reforms in official document processing. He stated that before reporting, he had something to declare: "Every time I give a report at the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, or the Administrative Yuan's weekly memorial meeting, it is either recorded by myself or by comrades, and after I have proofread and revised it, it is then released by the Central News Agency. The reports made on Mondays are usually published in the newspapers on Tuesdays. I am responsible for these drafts. However, evening newspapers in the capital often publish based on other records, which have not been corrected by me, leading to discrepancies from the original meaning. And because these are published first, various news agencies use them as a basis for dissemination at home and abroad, spreading inaccuracies. Although the original draft can be published the next day for correction, the inaccuracies of the previous day are enough to cause considerable unnecessary misunderstanding. Now, I solemnly declare once again that I am not responsible for any records that have not been proofread and revised by myself. Today, I have two things to report.

The first is the issue of diplomatic policy. Diplomatic policy is decided by the Central Government, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs merely executes the policies decided by the Central Government. The policies decided by the Central Government were stated in a telegraph sent jointly with Chairman Chiang, the most important meaning of which is that the people of the whole country must painfully and clearly recognize that China is currently in a position of accumulated weakness, not only weak but also in a position of being infringed upon. This position is an unprecedented national crisis for China. However, since the 19th century, there have been many countries and nations in the world that have encountered such national crises. Some have perished, while others have struggled to survive to this day. The form of national crisis varies from country to country, but the common ground is to clearly recognize one's own position in order to seek self-salvation and survival. There is no need to panic or be indignant. For example, France after the Franco-Prussian War and Germany after World War I are examples. France's famous saying at the time was, 'Keep it in your heart at all times, but not on your lips.' Germany was even more patient and hardworking, and it still is today. I once heard someone say, 'If we train 3,000 airplanes, we will definitely be able to take revenge.' This is simply nonsense. Do you have 3,000 airplanes now? Will they allow you to calmly train 3,000 airplanes? When you calmly train 3,000 airplanes, they will have already trained 4,000 or 5,000. What then? If the above three questions cannot be answered, then it is better not to say such nonsense. The ancients once said, 'He who has the intention of plotting against others and makes it known to others is in danger.' I don't mean it that way, because we only seek self-salvation and survival, not plotting against others. Perhaps we won't even have the time or opportunity to achieve self-salvation and survival. We should not slacken our determination as long as there is a breath of life left. Plotting against others is out of the question, and even more so is trying to collude with or seek help from others. I once said, 'Without considerable national strength, we cannot talk about resistance, nor can we talk about friendship.' In other words, 'Only by surviving can we coexist; without surviving, we will not be able to coexist.' Now, some people talk about a pro-A faction, and others talk about a pro-B faction. This is even more nonsense than before. The collusion on one side has not yet taken effect, while the conflict on the other side has already shown results. If we can clearly recognize our current position, we will never take such a risky move. We must know that our current position is like being critically ill. Apart from treating the symptoms, all food should be light. If we suddenly take tonics, it will not only not help the illness but may even hasten death. Colluding with or seeking help from others is like taking tonics before the illness has subsided. What could be more dangerous than this? Therefore, our diplomatic policy today is completely consistent with our domestic policy. The first sentence is to develop the people's strength and develop the people's productive capacity. The second sentence is also to develop the people's strength and develop the people's productive capacity. However, the purpose of development is to achieve self-salvation and survival. Therefore, we must have a detailed and prudent distinction and choice between what is urgent and what is not. This is what we should pay attention to.

The second thing is the Administrative Yuan's reform of official document processing.

Regarding the handling of official documents, I feel that past malpractices have had a great impact on administrative efficiency. Therefore, on June 20, at the Administrative Yuan's meeting, I proposed convening a review meeting to plan reforms. The reviewers included 14 agencies from the Administrative Yuan's Secretariat, Political Affairs Department, and various ministries. It lasted more than two months, with five meetings. All reviewers were able to work tirelessly, continuing their research under the scorching heat. The preliminary work was finally completed last Tuesday. This is something I truly admire.

Why is it necessary to reform the past procedures for handling official documents? Because administration is a specialized skill. Administration values efficiency the most, and to improve efficiency, we must modernize and rationalize administration. This cannot be achieved overnight. However, if we want politics to take on the new mission of the new era, we must first pay attention to various administrative reforms. Official document processing is one aspect of this.

The first drawback of past official document processing procedures is "delay." The reason for the delay is that the people handling the documents like to make them travel for a long time. Long-term travel can be divided into two types. One is going in circles, from agency A to agency B, from agency B to agency C, from agency C to agency D, and then back from agency D to agency A. This kind of circular travel is meaningless. The reason is that each agency procrastinates, leading to this phenomenon. The second is lingering along the way. A document is sent to agency A, where it is arbitrarily delayed for a few days, and then forwarded to agencies B, C, and D, each of which does the same. Things that could be resolved in one or two days are often delayed for one or two weeks or one or two months. The reason is that when agencies encounter official matters that cannot be delayed, they still refuse to take responsibility and handle them immediately, leading to this phenomenon. The reason why these two phenomena occur is entirely because the methods of official document processing are not reasonable, so those who are unwilling to handle things are happy not to handle them, and those who are willing to handle things are unable to do so. My first feeling was that at one meeting, I remembered an official matter that had been reviewed by various departments but had not been replied to for a long time. When I asked about the reason, I found out that because the nature of the matter required joint review by departments A, B, and C, the document was sent from the Administrative Yuan to the three departments, passing through the hands of clerks, section chiefs, secretaries, and counselors, and finally to the vice ministers and ministers, which took several days. It took several more days for the three departments to send out reviewers. It took several more days for the reviewers to report the results of their review to their superiors. It took several more days for the three departments to draft a reply to the Administrative Yuan. This already took two or three weeks. If the clerks arbitrarily delayed it from the beginning, it would take even more days. If one of the three departments could not send out a reviewer on time, it would take even more days. If the reviewers still had to ask their superiors for instructions, it would take even more days. Thus, two or three weeks or even two or three months would not be surprising. We realized that this method of long-term travel would ruin everything invisibly, so we reformed it immediately. For example, at the Yuan meeting on Tuesday, a certain official matter is assigned to departments A, B, and C for joint review, and personnel from the Yuan's Secretariat and Political Affairs Department are also assigned to participate, with a deadline of Friday of the same week to hold a review meeting at the Yuan. The reviewers obtain the opinions of their superiors in advance and attend the review. If the opinions are the same, the case is reviewed immediately, and it can be completed within a week. Sometimes the review opinions are not entirely the same, so a second review meeting is scheduled. It doesn't matter if a third, fourth, or fifth meeting is held. This is progress and meaningful, unlike long-term travel that is not progressive and meaningless. After we reformed this one official matter, we proceeded to reform all other similar official matters. In short, we changed from slow to fast, and the method is not to be perfunctory but to proceed responsibly. Because of responsible progress, the bad habits of going in circles and lingering along the way can be eliminated, and official documents will not suffer from long-term travel. This is the first point of reforming the procedures for handling official documents.

The second drawback of past official document processing procedures is "repetition." Many documents that do not need to be replied to are replied to as a matter of routine because there is no standard for not replying, which serves no other purpose than to expand the sales of paper stores. Now that we have set a standard for not replying to official documents, we can save a lot of time and resources.

The third point of reforming official document processing procedures is to use punctuation. Some people think this is unnecessary, but they don't know that without punctuation, the sentence structure is unclear, making approval difficult and reading prone to errors. At meetings, reading documents often leaves the reader confused and the listener baffled due to unclear sentence structure. Although it is more complicated for the person drafting the document to use punctuation, the time saved by the dozens of people who review the document is actually greater. Not only can it make official documents easier to review, but it can also avoid many unnecessary errors. I remember a story about a son who sent eight mooncakes to his father and wrote in the letter, "Sending eight mooncakes for father's use." Because there was no punctuation, it was originally "Sending eight mooncakes, for father's use." His father read it as "Sending eight mooncakes for father's use," and became suspicious, saying, "Eight fathers? I am one. Where can I find the other seven?" This is of course a joke, but there are actually similar jokes in judicial litigation cases. In the past, after a man's son died, he sent his daughter-in-law back to her parents' home in Ning and made a written statement saying, "You are allowed to go home and marry, but you are not allowed to come back and serve my parents." It was originally "You are allowed to go home and marry, but you are not allowed to come back and serve my parents." Later, a dispute arose, and it was read as "You are allowed to go home, but you are not allowed to marry and come back to serve my parents," and the meaning was completely reversed. These are all the drawbacks of not using punctuation. Although this is not a common occurrence, it shows the importance of punctuation.

The fourth point is official document inspection. Official documents are not only afraid of delay but also of being missed. This reform has strict inspection regulations to prevent official documents from being delayed or missed.

The fifth point is file organization. Because the previous methods of handling files were not good, the responsible officials often neglected the content of the cases and could not find them for reference. Now, there are regulations for setting up a general inspection card to allow the highest-level officials to know the entire content, like a library catalog, and the organization methods are set up to make it easy to check and find.

The above five points can be said to be the key points of this reform of official document processing. As for the detailed items, the regulations have been drafted, and those who participated in this review meeting can explain them to their colleagues in detail. Today, I am only briefly mentioning one or two to draw your attention. This reform only involves the scope of processing procedures and is only a starting point. As for the fundamental transformation of the official document format, we must continue to pay attention to it in order to achieve the final goal. This is what I hope for from my colleagues in the Yuan and all officials in the various ministries. Finally, there is one more point that I hope for from my colleagues. As I just said, making official documents travel for a long time is a common problem among officials at all levels. But in addition to this problem, there is an even bigger problem, which is to imprison official matters forever. Only the superiors have this power. A superior can approve, reject, revise, or review an official matter. These are all progressive. The only thing that should not be done is to neither reject nor revise nor submit for review, but to stuff it in the drawer of the desk. That is not progressive. The document is then imprisoned. This kind of imprisonment can last for a few weeks, a few months, or even indefinitely. That is why it is said to be imprisoned forever. This kind of imprisonment is not progressive. I have a belief about official matters: progress. Progress can be good or bad. Not progressing seems to be neither good nor bad, but everything is ruined invisibly, which can be said to be purely bad and absolutely unacceptable. I ask all my colleagues that if I ever imprison an official document, you must protest to me. Although the superior has authority, it can only be used for progressive purposes such as approving, rejecting, revising, and reviewing, and not for non-progressive purposes. I am deeply remorseful and want to remove these malpractices. Therefore, I sincerely ask all my colleagues to work together to remove these malpractices. These malpractices exist in all agencies. It is the fault of the superiors, not the fault of the subordinates. But if the subordinates constantly protest, then the superiors can at least commit fewer sins. This is the last thing I hope for from all my colleagues. (Central News Agency telegram on the 28th)

Central National Government

Two Memorial Week Reports 31

Duan Xipeng: Self-Salvation and Self-Strengthening

Shao Yuanchong: Yellow River Flood

(Nanjing) The Central Government held its 93rd Memorial Week at 8:00 AM on the 28th, attended by approximately 600 people including Central Committee members Chen Guofu, Li Jingzhai, Duan Xipeng, Hong Ludong, Wang Qi, Li Ciwen, Huang Jichen, and staff. Chen Guofu presided, and Duan Xipeng reported, stating that the environment China is currently facing is unprecedented in history, with internal disasters such as floods, droughts, and communist bandits, and external pressures from strong neighbors encroaching on our land and resources. Looking around the world, all countries are taking a narrow-minded nationalistic approach for their own rights, increasing armaments, raising tariffs, and engaging in extreme reaction. If these contradictions cannot be resolved, their impact on our country's future will be enormous. Therefore, our country's future encounters will be even worse than today. Our fundamental solution is not to ally with A or ally with B, but to be in a proactive position and seek a path of self-salvation and self-determination. Currently, we should pay attention to creating a good political order and strengthening national power. All comrades should firmly believe in the spirit and methods of our party's doctrine, seek new understanding, and lead the people to achieve the goal of self-salvation and self-strengthening. (Central News Agency telegram on the 28th)

(Nanjing) The National Government held its Memorial Week at 9:00 AM on the 28th, attended by approximately 400 people including Yu Youren, Wang Yongbin, Huang Musong, Wei Huai, and National Government staff. Chairman Lin led the ceremony, and Shao Yuanchong reported on the Yellow River flood, stating that the Yellow River is the birthplace of our country's culture and the area of abundant agricultural production in ancient times. However, in modern times, it has become a major problem for our country. Because the Yellow River has breached its banks and changed course many times, and the Yellow River water carries sediment, it is not suitable for irrigation and is prone to flooding, making it impossible to contain. But according to experts, the Yellow River water carries no more than 10% sediment, and the rest is only yellow soil, which is suitable for planting. If it can be utilized, it will not only be harmless but also beneficial. In the past, those who managed the river only sought to prevent breaches and protect against them, without seeking to dredge and guide the source, allowing it to flood at will. In recent years, with the development of science, human power can conquer nature. The Netherlands is a country that seeks excellence in water conservancy, boasting that "God created the sea, and the Dutch created the land." But we use extremely outdated methods to manage the Yellow River, so it is appropriate that we do not see its benefits and only see its harms. In recent years, the central government has not neglected water conservancy, but it has been managed separately by river basin, resulting in as many as six or seven water conservancy agencies, which cannot be unified in command, resulting in twice the effort for half the results. Recently, the central government decided to unify the national water conservancy agencies and make overall plans, which may be effective. Although floods are caused by natural disasters, human power can control them. I am making this report based on my personal feelings and ask those who manage the river to seek fundamental governance strategies and use scientific methods to harness this great natural force, guiding it to irrigate farmland, so that the provinces along the river can all become fertile areas, which will be of great benefit to the national economy, people's livelihood, and national culture. I also hope that national water conservancy can be planned as a whole to achieve the ideal results. (Central News Agency telegram on the 28th)

Xu Shiying Arrives in Nanjing

Preparing for Flood Relief 32

Shandong Relief Committee Requests Immediate Relief

(Jinan) Jiang telegraphed the Relief Committee, stating that the Shandong flood is particularly pitiable and that methods for raising large amounts of relief funds have been telegraphed to the Administrative Yuan and the Ministry of Finance for review. (Special telegram on the 28th)

(Nanjing) Xu Shiying arrived in Nanjing at noon on the 28th on the Jiang'an Wheel from Xun, to prepare for the Yellow River flood relief. Xu said that the Yellow River flood has affected nearly 40 counties in the provinces of Hebei, Shaanxi, Shandong, Henan, Jiangsu, and Anhui, affecting over 2 million people. He has submitted a request to the Yuan for immediate relief, which was accepted by the review committee convened by the Administrative Yuan last Saturday. It is planned to release immediate relief funds on the 28th, along with the 1 million yuan previously requested by the committee for Shaanxi and other provinces. However, due to the exhaustion of the national treasury, it is difficult to raise cash, so it is tentatively planned to issue public bonds to provide relief, which will be decided after discussion at the Yellow River flood relief meeting to be convened on the 30th. He will stay in Nanjing for two or three days and then go to Shanghai to assist in raising funds. The report that he will be transferred to head the judiciary is completely unfounded. (Special telegram on the 28th)

(Jinan) Xu Shiying telegraphed the Relief Committee, ordering them to immediately report the estimated area of the disaster area, the number of victims, and the property losses, broken down by county, as of the date of the telegram, as well as the extent of local relief efforts, so that relief can be planned in a unified manner. The committee replied by telegram, requesting immediate relief, as people would have starved to death by the time the investigation was completed. (Special telegram on the 28th)

Shandong Province Reduces Government Spending for Disaster Relief

Provincial Government Office Expenses Reduced by 3,000 per Month 33

Office Expenses of Each County Reduced by 20%

(Jinan) Han Fuqu issued a handwritten order today, effective from August, reducing the provincial government's office expenses by 3,000 per month, the office expenses of each department by 500 per month, and the monthly salaries of civil servants earning more than 50 yuan by 20%. The office expenses of each county will also be reduced by 20% for a period of five months. In addition, effective from September, the number of public security bureaus and militia in the disaster areas will be reduced by half, and the construction and education fees will be suspended. The monthly salaries of the mayor and staff in the district will be reduced by half for a period of six months in order to save funds for disaster relief. A circular was also issued stating that the Yellow River breach and flooding have turned the counties in western Shandong into a vast swamp. All prevention and relief efforts require huge sums of money. At a time when the people's livelihood is declining, it is difficult to add to the burden. The only way is to reduce spending to supplement the funds. In addition to the provincial Department of Industry, which has been decided by the political conference to be abolished to save funds, the counties should also earnestly reduce government spending in view of the heavy disaster situation to economize and meet urgent needs. (Special telegram on the 28th)

Shandong Western Flood Disaster Committee Appeals

Allocate Large Sums for Immediate Relief 34

(Jinan) The Shandong Western Flood Disaster Relief Committee telegraphed Lin Wang Jiang Wenri, stating that the Yellow River breach has spread to western Shandong, with the counties of Heze, Juye, Zhang, Juancheng, Yuncheng, Dingtao, Chengwu, Yanggu, Jinxiang, Jiaxiang, Yutai, as well as Caozhou and Puyang, all becoming swamps, with houses washed away and people displaced. Those who died in the water were carried away by the waves, and no one collected their rotting corpses. Those who were fortunate enough to survive were all sleeping in the open air and exposed to the elements, without security for the morning and evening. The pain and misery were truly unbearable to witness. As the autumn wind intensifies and diseases gradually spread, the only hope for survival for the dying disaster victims lies in the current emergency relief. It is important that the central government has dispatched experts to Shandong by plane to conduct surveys and plan the fundamental project of breaching the river. However, relief efforts cannot be delayed, otherwise, by the time the plans are made and consultations are held, the breach will not have been closed, and the victims will have all died. The members of this committee are concerned about their hometown and cannot bear to watch from the sidelines. We are making a desperate appeal, which is not like the groaning of someone without illness. The Shandong Provincial Government and various charitable organizations of the Relief Committee have successively allocated more than one million yuan for emergency relief. However, this is only a drop in the bucket and cannot solve the problem. We admire your compassion and concern for the people and dare to send a special telegram to appeal to you to allocate a large sum of money for immediate relief to save the lives of the people. Shandong Western Flood Disaster Relief Committee bows in anticipation of your orders. (Special telegram on the 28th)

Commentary

Welcoming Song 36

By Zi

Finance Minister and Vice President of the Executive Yuan, Song Ziwen, is returning home from Europe and will arrive in Shanghai today. Since leaving the country on April 18th, Mr. Song has traveled from the United States to Europe, spending more than four months abroad, visiting various important countries. His formal mission was to participate in the Washington Conference and attend the World Economic Conference. However, what we can actually know he has achieved is the establishment of a $50 million USD cotton and wheat loan in the United States and the technical cooperation negotiations with the League of Nations in Europe. There are many different opinions about the advantages and disadvantages of these two matters for China, and it is difficult to make a quick judgment. Their major relationship to China's economy in the future, and the impact on politics and diplomacy, is something that ordinary people can imagine. Will Mr. Song be able to use this loan and cooperation well to build China, or will the results not be as some people fear? The matter is still unpredictable, but it seems that there is no doubt that the people of the country have good intentions towards Mr. Song upon his return to the country.

The cotton and wheat loan is 50 million USD, equivalent to more than 200 million in national currency, which is a huge foreign debt. In view of the past uses of foreign debt, the people of the country have both joy and worry about the success of this loan. The authorities have repeatedly stated that it will be used in the production sector in order to save China's backward production industry. However, this still fails to fully dispel the doubts of the worriers. Now that Mr. Song has returned, how will he make the people of the country understand his policies and be relieved?

Technical cooperation between China and the League of Nations has been going on for three years. Mr. Song's trip to Europe this time has allowed it to be completed. The event itself is already past the discussion stage. It is only that the Japanese, who are hostile to China, are jealous and hateful, creating dangerous rumors of international co-management. The international situation after the failure of the Economic Conference also does not allow the people of the country to deeply believe in "non-political" resolutions. Mr. Song has been in charge of cooperation with the League of Nations for three years, and now that he has returned successfully, will he be able to concretely announce the plans for taking advantage and avoiding harm for the cooperation?

Mr. Song's return this time is being closely watched by China's enemies. On the reverse side, this has become a factor in most of the people of the country expressing good feelings towards Mr. Song. We sincerely hope that Mr. Song will be able to maintain the good feelings that the people of the country have for him in the future.

Pacific Society

Secret Talks Between China and Japan 37

Seeking Ways to Resolve Disputes Between the Two Countries

Chinese Representative Refuses to Issue Declaration Guaranteeing the Puppet State

Peng Fu 38

People at the Pacific Society today admitted that Chinese and Japanese representatives have held secret talks here many times, trying to draft a way to resolve the disputes between China and Japan. Although none of the representatives have the power to make binding guarantees on behalf of the government, it is believed that if a basis can be found, even a temporary agreement can be seriously considered in Nanjing and Tokyo. It is said that the result of the talks was the creation of several informal agreements, which have been tentatively agreed upon. However, the Chinese representative refused to agree to issue a general declaration mutually guaranteeing the integrity of the territory, as this would be tantamount to guaranteeing the current situation in Manchuria. As for the Pacific Society itself, it is happy that both sides have this kind of talk, because if it can lead to a final agreement, the association will have an outstanding achievement. It is said that the key figures in the association had already proposed this kind of talk before the representatives departed for the meeting in Peng Fu. (Guomin telegram on the 27th)

After Mr. Cai Song returns home

Our Country's Foreign Policy 39

Japanese Foreign Ministry Closely Monitors

Unease Felt Especially Regarding League of Nations Cooperation with Our Country

The Eastern Daily Predicts an Economic War May Be Unavoidable

(Tokyo) The Foreign Ministry authorities are paying close attention to how Song Ziwen's return to the country, after achieving many successes during his travels to European and American countries, will ultimately affect the National Government's policy towards Japan. Their views are as follows: ㈠ Song Ziwen, having obtained political and economic assistance from European and American countries, was refused permission to land in Japan while en route home. This act is highly noteworthy. ㈠ The dispute between China and Japan in the League of Nations has been resolved due to Japan's withdrawal from the League. At this time, requesting assistance from the League would only provoke Japan. Moreover, the engagement of Dr. Leith-Ross to come to China requires Japan's close attention. However, there is no need for excessive action regarding Song's personal activities at the moment. If the National Government continues its policy towards Japan after Song's return, Japan should adopt the most appropriate measures. Therefore, there is a widespread emphasis on a serious attitude to monitor the development of the situation. (28th Dispatch from the Electric Communication Society)

(Tokyo) Finance Minister Song consistently refused to meet with Japanese reporters within Japanese territorial waters. The Eastern Daily comments on the situation after Finance Minister Song's return to China, stating that while Finance Minister Song was still in the United States, Huang Fu, Wang Jingwei, and Chiang Kai-shek had already convened in Lushan to discuss policies towards Japan. The situation in North China will not undergo any changes due to Song's return. Considering the future of Japan's domestic economy, Finance Minister Song, having secured support from Europe and America, may be even more determined to wage an economic war against Japan upon his return, raising tariffs and enacting new anti-dumping tariff laws to initiate a more intense tariff war with Japan. This kind of policy may be difficult to avoid. As for armed resistance, the Finance Ministry under Song is unlikely to advocate for reckless action. However, regarding an economic war, Japanese goods facing challenges from all sides, resulting in greater economic hardship, can be considered an expected outcome. (28th Dispatch from the China United Press)

Japanese Cabinet Seeks Aid from Political Parties

Saitō Meets with Adachi 43

President of Kokumin Dōmei Conspires to Slightly Oppose the Party

Seiyūkai Decides on National Policy Cooperation Direction

Yokohama 44

Prime Minister Saitō, returning from Hayama to Tokyo, visited Adachi, the president of Kokumin Dōmei, at the Hasseiden Hall in Honmoku, Yokohama, at 8:00 a.m. today. He reported on the progress of his meetings with the presidents of the Seiyūkai and Minseitō parties, and expressed his hope that Kokumin Dōmei would also assist the government with a spirit of national unity. President Adachi questioned him, asking whether he had concrete plans for national unity to overcome the extraordinary situation. The Prime Minister replied that he did not have any yet, but would create them in the future. President Adachi then expressed his personal opinion, saying that when he was the Minister of Communications in the past, the Seiyūkai and Minseitō parties, who opposed his views, now sending cabinet members was a form of national unity, which he found deeply moving. Now, the extraordinary situation has intensified, and due to the breakdown of the economic conference, external relations are subject to increased pressure in British colonies. Therefore, given this situation, it is likely that difficult times will be encountered even before 1936. National unity is something to be supported.

However, party leaders seeking party interests and wanting to pretend at national unity are being rejected by the public because the public is rejecting political parties. If we do not make a decisive move and establish major national policies, it will be difficult to easily agree to the government's policies. He hoped that they would review the platform printed by Kokumin Dōmei. Later, President Adachi added that he wanted to revise the election law and guide thought, but the Ministry of Interior's plan did not meet these hopes. Even the proportional representation system could not prevent improper behavior. Saitō returned to Tokyo after the meeting. (28th Dispatch from the Electric Communication Society)

(Tokyo) After Prime Minister Saitō met with President Suzuki, key figures in the Seiyūkai, Yamamoto Jōtarō and other committee members, repeatedly discussed concrete methods for cooperating on national policies. Currently, there are three broadly predictable methods: ㈠ President Suzuki joins the Cabinet as a Minister without Portfolio. ㈡ The government establishes a National Policy Deliberation Council, with Suzuki as a member. ㈢ The Seiyūkai sends representatives to negotiate with the government on various policies each time. The Seiyūkai does not favor the first option of a Minister without Portfolio. Regarding the second option of establishing a National Policy Deliberation Council, the government has already started preparing the budget for the next fiscal year, and it is practically impossible to add the Seiyūkai's opinions. The third method allows the Seiyūkai's opinions to be expressed earlier, so the Seiyūkai's opinion roughly settles on this third method of representative negotiation. (28th Dispatch from the Japan United Press)

(Tokyo) Since the Japanese government started the September 18th Incident and greatly increased its military activities in China, military spending has increased daily. In the current situation,

it seems there is no way to stop it. The financial community is greatly worried about the pressure of military expenses on public finances in the future. For this year's and next year's budgets, it is planned to issue 2 billion yen in public bonds. For the 1935 budget, due to the desire to compete in armaments with Britain and the United States, there is no way to reduce it. Regarding public bond policy, Finance Minister Takahashi expressed his views as follows: ㈠ Public bonds are divided into three types: one is military public bonds, for which a separate public bond law will be established to regulate their issuance; the second is public bonds for productive enterprises, which will be managed within the scope of the Public Enterprise Promotion Bond Law; and the third is deficit public bonds, which will be used to cover financial shortfalls. Regardless of how they are categorized, the total amount will only increase. ㈡ The policy of fiscal expansion will continue to be adopted, with all public bonds being acquired by the Bank of Japan. ㈢ Interest rates will be gradually reduced, with a repayment period of 20 or 30 years. Cottonseed Pills

Can Treat Illnesses and Provide Sustenance 49

New Invention by German Professor Schmid 50

Reuters Berlin Correspondence: Using pills for sustenance, originally an ideal, is now becoming a reality. This is the result of five years of intensive research by Professor Schmid of the University of Heidelberg in Germany. Rich nutrients are extracted from cottonseed and administered to patients, with excellent results. The extracted substance is similar to yellow powder and contains vitamins A, B, C, and E; the only missing vitamin is D, which can be added. Cottonseed extract contains 50% protein and 7.5% minerals. Its use on hospital patients has shown that it is truly a new way to nourish humans and may cause a revolution in health maintenance. According to medical reports, administering one spoonful of this substance daily to patients, either directly or added to other foods, for three months not only helps those suffering from malnutrition, but also those suffering from diabetes, kidney disease, heart disease, bile disorders, and tuberculosis to

gain weight and experience significant improvements in their mental state. Doctors now believe that cottonseed extract can also prevent cancer, as the medical community increasingly diagnoses cancer as originating from malnutrition. According to records, no patients taking cottonseed extract have experienced any adverse effects. Furthermore, because it is a powder, it is especially convenient for patients who cannot take pills. This substance is also an essential ingredient in skin disease treatments. There are many ways to consume it, and its benefits are immense. Therefore, cotton-producing countries can now add a great new industry of health products. Cottonseed extract can be added to cream, cheese, bread, ice cream, and candy, and to beverages such as wine, coffee, milk, and cocoa, increasing their nutritional value by 20% to 30%. According to chemical tests, fermentation and yeast are greatly enhanced by adding a small amount of cottonseed extract. Professor Schmid, the inventor of this substance, claims that two cottonseed pills a day can replace three meals. In the future, this substance can become the "iron ration" for soldiers, explorers, long-distance pilots, and civilians during food shortages. The state of Baden will soon begin testing cottonseed pills on schoolchildren, with official doctors closely monitoring the results. The Italian government is also paying attention to Schmid's invention and plans to develop cotton fields in its colonies. Schmid completed his experiments in Egypt. Schmid's products are now sold in Egyptian markets. The Chinese and Japanese governments are also inquiring about Schmid's invention and the results of his experiments.

Roosevelt's Private Residence

British and American Roundtable Talks Held 51

To Discuss Stabilizing Exchange Rates 52

Precursor to Cooperation Between the Pound and the Dollar 53

Hyde Park 54

Norman, the Governor of the Bank of England, and Harrison, the Governor of the New York Federal Reserve Bank, are scheduled to meet with President Roosevelt tomorrow. They will participate in a roundtable discussion with other international economic experts, primarily focusing on the duel between the British pound and the U.S. dollar. (27th Dispatch from Reuters)

(Washington) According to reliable sources, after a detailed investigation of the currency opinions of members of Congress, the US President believes that if prices and public purchasing power do not increase, a bill to force monetary inflation will be passed after Congress reconvenes in January next year. Therefore, he intends to earnestly handle this matter in early autumn to prevent Congress from having plans to disrupt industry and commerce. Roughly, after meeting with Norman, the Governor of the Bank of England, within this week, he will convene the Brain Trust to create a plan to further increase purchasing power. As for the meeting between the US President and Norman, Wall Street bankers in New York and economic experts in Washington all say that the President is prepared to discuss stabilizing the gold standard, as he believes that the progress of the industrial recovery plan has guaranteed an increase in purchasing power. With increased purchasing power, prices will naturally rise, negating the need for large-scale monetary inflation. It is heard that Undersecretary of the Treasury Acheson, President of the New York Federal Reserve Bank Harrison, and others have prepared reports on foreign trade, price levels, and the success of the recovery plan for reference during the meeting. According to Wall Street sources, the US President will discuss with Norman the feasibility of establishing a currency stabilization fund. (27th Dispatch from the National News Agency)

New York Plans to Establish a Free Gold Market 55

(Washington) According to sources close to the US government, France is currently under pressure from many sides to abandon the gold standard. As a result of this pressure, the US government may be able to open gold in New York and establish a free trading market. In recent weeks, although European gold standard countries have strengthened their gold positions through cooperation between central banks, the pressure on the Netherlands has not eased slightly. The ongoing battle has caused world gold prices to be higher than in the United States. If European countries are unable to maintain this struggle, the United States can establish a free gold trading market without fear of disrupting currency and finance. According to treasury officials, the US Department of Justice's campaign to force gold hoarders to surrender their gold has failed, and the gold coins and gold certificates currently scattered among the people are the fewest in fifty years. According to a Treasury Department investigation, the whereabouts of only 57.4 million US dollars in gold coins and gold certificates are currently unknown. It is estimated that most of them have been destroyed, lost, or smuggled to Europe. Although there are huge amounts of gold that are known to be hoarded privately, the whereabouts of most of the others are unknown. Therefore, the government's gold position is excellent. Regardless of where those scattered abroad go, they are unlikely to have a disruptive effect on finance. As for what actions the government will take against known gold hoarders, nothing has been heard today. (28th Dispatch from the National News Agency)

France Has No Intention of Abandoning the Gold Standard 56

(Paris) The decline in the value of British and American currencies is now causing unease among French financiers, but most public opinion believes that France will not abandon the gold standard unless forced to. Currently, France's gold reserves reach 79.62%, and the public feels that France is not worried about the currency devaluation of other countries, because most of France's business is in French colonies. France's biggest danger lies in balancing the French budget. It is found that the French budget is short 60 billion francs. There is little hoarding of cash other than by the Bank of France. Although trade is not smooth, it is still satisfactory. The general public is paying close attention to tomorrow's meeting between bankers and Roosevelt. (27th Dispatch from Reuters)

Britain Doubts Roosevelt's Policies 57

(London) Since the United States implemented "the experiment of the New Economic Policy," the major British newspapers have daily criticized President Roosevelt's policies in editorials or special articles. Initially, British public opinion was quite favorable. Londoners believed that the leader of the American Democratic Party had a strong reputation for liberalism abroad and could understand the actual situation in the international arena. Hearing of his election, they were all delighted, admiring his character. Therefore, they also expressed sympathy for his policies. At the beginning of March this year, Roosevelt's plan was to make domestic and foreign affairs mutually coordinated, that is, to engage in rescuing the economy from panic internally, and to advocate cooperation with various countries externally to solve world economic problems. Providing the Allied nations with a favorable solution to the war debt problem was also included. Unexpectedly, after a period of time, the American attitude greatly disappointed people. The biggest problem left by the European war (referring to war debts) has been delayed and not resolved. From the perspective of the debtor nations, it must be resolved as soon as possible, but the United States ultimately considers it a secondary issue and will only consider it after the American domestic economy recovers. The return of American policy to nationalism can be seen here. However, British people only expressed disappointment about this. Until the eve of the opening of the Economic Conference and after it had already opened, the American representatives refused to sign the declaration on stabilizing currencies as many as three times, and the argument was greatly angered. Generally, people believe that if measures are to be taken to rescue the economy from panic, currency should first be stabilized. Even if it cannot be said that rescue cannot be discussed without this, the importance of its relationship is undeniable. However, the United States stubbornly refused to do so, and the agitation of people's hearts can be imagined. The disagreement between the United States and general opinion fortunately relied on the mediation of representatives of various autonomous territories, and emotional relationships began to get closer. Those who defend the United States must say that Britain has not also experienced the devaluation of the pound and monetary inflation? This is true, but the reason for Britain's so is the natural result of the situation, not that

Britain intended to make it so. Britain has used the method of the de facto stable pound, reorganized the economy, and established an adjustment fund to prevent monetary inflation, rescue the pound from falling, and prevent planned changes in various currencies. This is obvious to all. Since the close of the Economic Conference, British people have been gradually observing "the experiment of the American New Economic Policy." No change, no matter how big or small, has been missed. Public opinion towards the United States has changed from sympathy to criticism, and then the concept of interests and harms has risen from criticism. Extending to the present, most people feel that Roosevelt has faced the greatest difficulty of "raising prices," so they cannot help but express doubt about his policies. However, most people still quietly watch the success or failure and use humorous words to comfort themselves, saying, "We should not take two steps forward at the same time. Only after the first step is successful can there be a second step. Now, it is not yet known whether the first step will be successful, so we should not rush to take the second step." The Secretary of the Treasury is currently studying the facts in order to find a way. (27th Dispatch from Havas)

US Auto Industry Code Signed

Another Obstacle Removed from the Recovery Plan 58

Hyde Park 59

President Roosevelt has signed the auto industry code, which stipulates weekly working hours from 35 to 48 hours and minimum hourly wages from 40 to 43 cents. Although auto industry tycoon Ford did not participate in the preparation of this industry code, the industry code is a concession to Ford. The industry code does not mention price limits, and allows manufacturers to hire workers and give them promotions and demotions based on their performance, regardless of which union they belong to. The labor side accepts this clause, with the understanding that it does not prejudice collective bargaining and a reservation against including this clause in any other industry code. Of the 40 million workers in the country, 15 million are now working under industry codes, and 18 industries are self-governing under federal supervision. The National Industrial Recovery Act Execution Office now estimates that 2 million automatic resumption-of-work agreements have been signed. (27th Dispatch from Reuters)

Germans Do Not Forget the Saar 63

130,000 People Express Loyalty to the Motherland

Paris Seems Rather Uneasy

Reuters 27th Paris Dispatch: Today, more than 50,000 residents of the Saar region went to Niedewod, South Prussia, to express their loyalty to their German motherland. Because in 1935 the Saar region will vote to decide whether the region will continue to be administered by the League of Nations, or whether it will be incorporated into France or Germany, the National Socialist Party is actively promoting it. It is heard that the chairman of the Saar Governing Commission will file a protest with the League of Nations against the National Socialist Party's propaganda. Paris also seems rather uneasy about this matter.

National News Agency 28th Rutesheim Dispatch: 30,000 Germans came by special train from the Saar region, and another 100,000 people came from all over Germany, all gathered in front of the historical monument in Nittelwald, overlooking the Rhine River, to express their loyalty to Germany. Prime Minister Hitler gave a speech to the gathering, saying, "We have repeatedly stated that we do not want to and do not want to incorporate the lands of other countries into Germany. However, our enemies must be made to respect treaties. The people of the Saar will vote in 1935 to decide which country they wish to belong to. I know that everyone will vote to support the motherland. Germany will never abandon the Saar region, and the Saar region will never turn its back on Germany. One day, the Saar region will return to the German motherland, and there will be no greater joy in our lives than this."

National News Agency 27th Rutesheim Dispatch: After participating in the Danlenburg Memorial Ceremony, German Prime Minister Hitler took a large plane to Berlin to meet with about 100 German aviators who had just completed the 1933 Air Race. After a short rest, he took a plane to Rutesheim and went to the monument to give a speech to the crowd.

Bolivian-Paraguayan Dispute

Four Countries Ask the United States to Arbitrate 64

National News Agency 27th Asunción Dispatch: Diplomats from Argentina, Brazil, Chile, and Peru have drafted a method for resolving the basic issues in the dispute between Paraguay and Bolivia, advocating first asking the US Supreme Court for arbitration. If the Supreme Court refuses to arbitrate or cannot mediate, then they will ask the International Court of Justice in The Hague for arbitration. However, according to the Constitution, the US Supreme Court has no right to arbitrate disputes between two foreign countries. Therefore, it is now planned to first inquire in Washington whether any of the judges of the Supreme Court are willing to arbitrate for the two countries. According to the opinions of the four neutral countries' diplomats, there are only two basic issues in the Chaco Valley dispute: ㈠ Bolivia, lacking a sea outlet, wants to obtain a sea route through the Pilcomayo River and the Paraguay River in the Chaco Valley. ㈡ Both countries want to obtain a portion of the Chaco Valley. The purpose of the war is only to gain more land. However, the US Supreme Court's litigation is usually very complicated, and since the United States is one of the neutral committee members and has not been able to find a solution before, it is feared that it may not be able to mediate. Therefore, it is expected that this case will ultimately be submitted to the Hague Court.

The content includes: (A) General Review, (I) Administrative laws and regulations, (II) Management of international trade, (III) Regulations on the manufacture, sale, distribution and consumption of medicines, (IV) Matters concerning international cooperation; (B) Special Drugs, (V) Raw opium and coca leaves, (VI) Prepared opium, (I) Statistics of opium addiction hospitals and number of patients in each province, (II) Statistics of the number of people and fines handled by various courts in opium cases, (III) Statistics of opium and drug paraphernalia confiscated by various courts, (X) Indian hemp, (VII) Medicinal opium, morphine, cocaine, heroin, etc., with statistics of legal imports of various medicines this year, (VIII) Illegal trafficking, (I) Statistics of drugs seized by various customs, (II) Statistics of the amount of drugs smuggled by foreigners, (III) Statistics of the sources of drugs, (IV) Statistics of the number of foreigners smuggling, (V) Statistics of foreign ships smuggling drugs; (C) Miscellaneous Records, (X) Fulfillment of international opium suppression treaty obligations, (X)(I) Others, (X)(II) Conclusions and recommendations, etc. (Central News Agency Telegram from the 28th)

Jiangsu-Zhejiang Sericulture Control Association

Planning Silk Improvement Measures 74

(Nanjing) In recent years, the silk industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang has been affected by rayon, plummeting drastically. The Executive Yuan has repeatedly received requests from various parties to continue issuing the remaining two million of the public bonds for the relief of the silk industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. At the same time, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, together with the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, were ordered to properly plan for fundamental improvement and relief measures. So far, the public bonds have not been issued. According to Dong Xiujia, the silkworms raised by farmers this year have had a very good harvest, especially the improved silkworm cocoons, which are of good quality and white in color, selling for forty to fifty yuan per dan. As for the two million public bonds, the Ministry of Finance has not approved their issuance due to fund issues, but they are not needed at the moment. As for fundamental relief, it will start with improving silkworm seed and sericulture. Now that the results of improved seeds are good, efforts should be made to promote them so that people can adopt improved seeds. Mulberry trees are also being purchased and distributed to farmers for planting. Although the decline of the silk industry in recent years has been affected by the dumping of foreign goods, the poor quality of the silk itself is also the biggest reason. This fundamental improvement plan is currently being carried out by the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Sericulture Control Association. (Special Dispatch from the 28th)
