Japanese Immigrants and Officials in the Northeast 91

丨Protecting Exploitation with Troops丨

Harbin Correspondence: It has been almost two years since Japan seized Manchuria. During these two years, coupled with the Rehe War, we, travelers in a foreign land, not only have witnessed the tyranny of Japanese imperialism, implementing its "way of destruction," but also have personally tasted the flavor of the "way of destruction."

Everyone who has been to the Northeast has seen the methods by which the Japanese invaded the Northeast and knows the means they use. Since the so-called Manchurian state was established, the situation has changed even more. In the past, China still retained an empty name, at least we Chinese could walk and speak more conveniently. Now, it's different. The superficial order (limited to cities along the railway lines) seems to be better, but the so-called bandits of the Japanese, which from the perspective of the Chinese nation are volunteer armies, are still emerging unpredictably, especially in various parts of northern Manchuria, and along the Jihui Line, they are extremely fierce. The Kwantung Army Headquarters once boasted that order had been restored and that they could live a peaceful life from now on. In fact, the so-called restoration and the so-called peace are only in a few large cities on the South Manchuria Railway or Dalian, and other places are not included. As for places thirty or forty miles away from the railway, there is no peace. When the Japanese army first arrived in the Northeast, it tried its best to seize power, so the main force was concentrated in a few large cities and forcibly seized several mines, seizing the industries operated by Chinese capital, which made the social economy of the three northeastern provinces even more decline. At the same time, this method cannot solve the economic panic in Japan. So it changed its policy, from the city to the countryside, and implemented its armed immigration policy. Everyone knows that the place where it immigrates is Jiamusi on the Songhua River, because this is the most fertile and suitable place for rainfall in the northern Manchurian region, and there are many virgin lands to be reclaimed. Chinese people have also put a lot of effort there and have opened up many places, so the Japanese specifically proposed it as their immigration test area. Last October, the first batch of 500 immigrants arrived in Jiamusi. They all carried rifles and were equipped with an appropriate number of bullets, but without family members. Judging from the current situation, I am afraid that they will not be able to bring their family members in the end. The reasons are: First, daily life there is unstable, and volunteer armies often come in and out. This kind of army specializes in making things difficult for the Japanese, which makes them unable to settle down and cultivate the land. Second, the weather is too cold. In winter, it can be as cold as minus forty degrees. They have to live in the house for almost half a year. The Japanese are already not used to this kind of life, and Japanese women don't even need to be mentioned. Third, diet is also very inconvenient. People who are used to eating rice, how can they eat sorghum? Even if they eat white noodles every day, it is still a hard thing. Since life has such troubles, and their purpose in going there is for life, so in less than half a year, 50 out of 500 people openly lagged behind, and more than 110 people fled back to Japan. Only 300 people remained. The second batch of armed immigrants could not recruit enough 500 people in Japan, and as a result, only 450 people arrived in Jiamusi in July of this year. This group of immigrants is generally not as good as last year's in terms of spirit. However, their organization is more meticulous, and the use of weapons is more flexible. In addition to reclaiming land, they also use the cover of political power to seize the land of Chinese farmers for their (immigrants') farming needs. Some repay a few tenths of the land price, giving a price of one to three yuan per hectare. Some even use military force to forcibly take it, regardless of whether you sell it or not, and just take it directly. The oppressed and honest Chinese farmers, what else can they say, and where dare they say anything?

They occupy the land of the Chinese and use it as their own land for Japanese self-cultivating farmers. At present, Japanese immigrants are building shrines, building hospitals, and reforming the agricultural tools used by the Chinese. The immigration policy that has been advocated for many years has taken more than a year. In addition to the farmers themselves having guns, a considerable amount of troops must be stationed in the surrounding counties and towns to protect them. More than 20,000 troops are stationed along the Middle East Road. In fact, they only protect 700 immigrants. From this, we cannot but say that their immigration policy is not a failure, but they still have places to seek compensation. The first is the income from the South Manchuria Railway and the industries along the South Manchuria Railway, as well as the railways built by Chinese capital seized after the September 18 Incident, such as the Taoang Road, the Feng Hai Road, and the Da Tong Road, etc., have all become the property of the South Manchuria Railway. The second is that industries operated by Chinese people, such as mines and factories, are often confiscated under the pretext of anti-Manchurian crimes.

Although Japanese immigration has failed, in addition to seeking compensation economically, they also have their movement of officials politically. The hotels in Shenyang and Changchun (opened by the Japanese) are full of people every day, all coming to find official positions. Now, in every county office, in addition to a puppet who is a fake countryman, there is another Japanese who acts as a councilor. In fact, the Japanese councilor (some say he is an instructor) has full authority, but he cannot arrange for a large number of officials from Japan to be placed (the total number of Japanese officials already employed in the four northeastern provinces is more than 1,500), and there are more than 2,000 living in hotels. Therefore, the puppet state's General Affairs Office is planning to divide each county into four or five districts, and each district will be assigned a councilor or instructor, all of whom are Japanese with dual nationality, to supervise the puppet county magistrate and rule the people. The exploitation and corruption of these people is more shameless and fierce than the old bureaucrats who used to care about face. Therefore, the slaves who used to express goodwill to Japan are now gradually feeling some remorse, but unfortunately, there is a lack of opportunity to serve the motherland. (August 22)

Water Conservancy Expert Wu Tongju's Letter to Li Xie

Statement of Opinions on Governing the Yellow River 92

In addition to embankment projects, industrial revitalization should also be implemented.

Zhenjiang Correspondence: The Yellow River's breach and flood disaster is expanding. Although the summer flood season has passed, the autumn flood season is approaching rapidly. If the embankment projects at various breach points are not expedited, the consequences will be dire. In light of this, water conservancy expert Wu Tongju recently sent a letter to Li Xie (Yizhi), Chairman of the Yellow River Water Conservancy Commission, outlining fundamental plans for comprehensively repairing all embankments, increasing the construction of stone dams, and other measures. He further advocated that, in addition to construction projects, industrial revitalization should also be implemented. If revitalization can be integrated into the projects, costs can be reduced and benefits expanded. The letter, consisting of over a thousand words, is recorded below: "To Mr. Yizhi, I was deeply concerned upon hearing of your illness in Xi'an this spring and summer. Later, upon meeting Brother Xu Jiachen, I was relieved to learn that you have largely recovered, but remain weak and require recuperation. This year, the Yangtze River experienced high floods, but was protected due to the completion of embankment works. Unexpectedly, the Yellow River has overflowed, causing multiple breaches in Lankao, Changdong, and several other counties, resulting in an expanding disaster. I was shocked to hear the news. Fortunately, the main channel has not been diverted, but the flooding has already submerged hundreds of miles of land on both the north and south banks. The autumn flood season is long, and the consequences of unblocked breaches are unimaginable. Yesterday, I received a provincial order to investigate the Lankao breaches, but the trip was canceled due to the easing situation. Instead, I went to your commission and the Huai River Commission to inquire about everything. I met Vice Chairman Wang, who indicated that a plan was already in place, mentioning that the Yellow River is too wide in some areas and needs to be narrowed with long embankments, straightened bends, and that the estuary needs to be dredged. These are indeed fundamental plans. Recently, I also read the telegrams from Vice Chairman Wang and Brother Jiachen, which clearly distinguished between priorities. Today's newspapers reported your telegram to the Executive Yuan, which demonstrates your balanced and objective perspective on the overall situation. This matter is only about prioritizing tasks, not about right or wrong. We share the same concerns. Now that you have arrived in Nanjing for meetings, concrete solutions should be reached soon. There is no need for lengthy discussions. In my opinion, there are many post-disaster issues that need to be addressed, and the most important and urgent is the issue of closing the breaches. This major embankment project requires your leadership. Given your position, no one else is suitable. For the embankment project, the old method of 'soft embankment' can be adopted, which is easier to implement. In the past, the Gongjia breach in Shandong Province adopted a new method of piling and stonework, which was ultimately risky. I believe you are aware of this. For today's situation, advance preparation is crucial: First, 'Recruit talent.' Shandong and Henan provinces have more experienced Yellow River workers than Hebei. Appointing the right person to manage the breach closure is critical. If the right person is found, the task will be half completed with twice the result. Second, 'Prepare materials.' In the past, embankment closures in the East River often used *ji*. With the current flooding on both banks, the *ji* may be rotten and unusable. It may be necessary to purchase and transport materials from afar. Other materials such as [missing text] are also required in large quantities and must be fully stocked to avoid delays. The above is very important. With sufficient preparation, work can begin immediately. Before starting work, it is necessary to assess the direction of the main channel near the breaches, select a location for the [missing text] and determine the platform in preparation for occupying it. It may be necessary to first [missing text] water to [missing text] to prevent the closure from becoming more difficult. After the closure, [missing text] embankment, replenish the main embankment, build ring embankments, and add support embankments, or fill in the breaches and build dam piles, all of which have established precedents. Special attention should be paid to guarding against ice floods and peach blossom floods in dangerous and remote areas, and sufficient materials should be prepared. If the breach closes naturally, as in the case of the Liu Zhuang breach in Dongming in 1926, it will be easier to build a main embankment. Currently, floodwaters are still rising from time to time, and there are many dangerous works in Henan and Shandong provinces. These can be entrusted to the river affairs bureaus of the two provinces to take charge separately. You can focus on closing the breaches, which will be easier and more effective. However, the great task of governing the Yellow River is not limited to closing breaches. It is also necessary to plan for fundamental solutions: First, comprehensively repair all embankments. Jia Rang's three policies referred to Yu the Great and set high goals. Since the Qin and Han dynasties, they have not been applicable. The achievements of Pan Jixun and Jin Fu in the Ming and Qing dynasties were based on the lowest of Jia Rang's three policies: repairing the old embankments, increasing the height and thickness of weak and damaged sections. The entire system is diseased, and unless a comprehensive repair is undertaken now, repeated flooding will continue year after year, resulting in endless labor and expense. In past dynasties, there were examples of increasing the height of the embankments by five inches each year and undertaking a major repair every few years. Since the founding of the Republic of China, twenty years have passed without annual repairs, and major repairs cannot be further delayed. Second, increase the construction of stone dams. East of Mengjin, the soil is loose and the water flows freely. The main river embankments have repeatedly failed. In the Guangxu period of the Qing dynasty, Henan Province began to use stone paving to protect the embankment slopes, which was very effective. The crushed stone dams were particularly effective. In recent years, Shandong Province has followed suit, but it is difficult to transport stone in the Puyang and Fanxian areas due to their distance from the mountains. Changyuan and Dongming have not yet implemented this measure. The junction of Henan, Hebei, and Shandong provinces is extremely dangerous and requires more crushed stone dams to deflect the floodwaters and provide protection. This can be compared to the T-head groynes invented by German engineer Engels. American engineer Freeman also advocated guiding the water flow in the central channel, which is the same idea. This year's Yellow River disaster provides a major lesson: embankments without dams are the same as having no embankments. With the completion of the dam works, the main embankment will be permanently secure. Third, dredge the estuary. This issue is the most difficult to address. The Southern River Party has repeatedly discussed the estuary. The water flows freely upon reaching the estuary, and human efforts are difficult to implement. Neither the "Water Dragon" nor the "Iron Rib" have been very effective. The only method is to continue building long embankments to confine the water and attack the sand. I have often examined the Yellow River situation in Henan, Hebei, and Shandong provinces. In Henan and Hebei provinces, the river channel is wide, with the distance between the two embankments ranging from ten to forty miles. To the north, there is the Taihang embankment and the ancient Great Jin embankment as a major barrier, which is strategically advantageous, but still cannot prevent flooding due to the disrepair of the embankments. On the south bank, there is only the official embankment and no [missing text] embankment, so there are many dangerous works on the south bank. Further downstream in Shandong Province, from Puyang, Li Sheng Tun to Shouzhang and Dongping, the Jin embankment serves as the official embankment on the north, and there is also a large official embankment on the south, with a distance of up to fifty or sixty miles between the two embankments. However, near the river, there are people's embankments only two or three miles wide, which seems to be too tight. From Dong'e to Licheng, there is a mountain range to the south as a barrier, and there are also people's embankments within the official embankment to the north, making the river channel narrow and constricted. From Licheng to Lijin, the official embankment is guarded to the south, and the people's embankment is guarded to the north. North of the people's embankment, there was an official embankment, but it has been abandoned for a long time, and the river channel is still narrow. Below Lijin, there are only people's embankments, ending at Tie Menguan. In general, the problem lies in the people's embankments. If the people's embankments are to be abolished, it will be difficult to relocate the people, and it is not permitted by the facts. The river flows in the people's embankments, constrained on the left and right. If the lower reaches are blocked, the upper reaches will overflow, which is inevitable. When the tail escapes the embankments, the water flows freely and naturally. If the flow is weak, it will be even less smooth downstream. As a result, the water within the embankments of Henan, Hebei, and Shandong provinces is confined, and river disasters occur. Currently, there are more than ten channels in the Tie Menguan area, which change every year and have a poor shape. Allowing them to develop naturally will lead to siltation and a rising estuary. Without an outlet, the water will inevitably divert north to seize the Zhang and Wei rivers and south to seize the Si and Huai rivers. There are historical precedents for this, which is alarming. So, what can be done? The only solution is to build embankments to confine the water, as suggested by Vice Chairman Wang. However, there are concerns that the soil is not firm and the embankments will easily collapse, ultimately making it impossible to contain the water, so the effect is uncertain. The above three matters cannot be accomplished without large sums of money. Whether the Yellow River Commission can overcome these difficulties, I believe you have already planned. There is one more thing, that is, in addition to construction projects, revitalization must also be implemented, which is also important. Raising large sums of money to relieve the people's hunger and suffering is not your official responsibility, but the facts are intertwined, so you cannot ignore it. Even in terms of construction, raising funds for construction is likely to be very difficult, which is foreseeable. In my humble opinion, if revitalization can be integrated into the construction projects, costs can be reduced and benefits expanded. A Yellow River Construction and Revitalization Committee could be organized by the central government to take charge of the matter, with the Premier of the Executive Yuan as chairman and the Minister of Finance as vice-chairman, which would have greater strength and smoother progress. This is a once-in-a-century undertaking. I hope you will consider it carefully. However, if the Yellow River Commission can be established on a regular basis and authorized by the central government, there is no need to start anew. Benefiting the country and the people is within sight. I wrote this hastily late at night and hope you will consider it."

The Desolate Scene of Baotou 93

Sun Dianying's Troops Prepare to Move West

Heavy Taxes and a Pessimistic Outlook for Business

Baotou Correspondence: Sun Dianying's troops have been ordered to enter Qinghai for land reclamation and are departing from Chahar, concentrating in the Baotou and Sayan areas to prepare for their journey to Qinghai. This unit is the 9th Army Corps of North China, consisting of three armies. In addition to the original 41st Army, there is the 55th Army and the newly formed Cavalry Army. Sun Dianying himself concurrently serves as the commander of the 41st Army. The 55th Army is formed by transferring a part of the original 55th Army and the 5th Regiment of the 41st Army stationed in Jincheng. The Cavalry Army is formed by the two cavalry divisions from the old Rehe, with Yu Shiming as the commander. Sun Dianying is currently in Taiyuan and will inspect the troops stationed in Jincheng within days. According to Yu Shiming, "Our army fought against the Japanese in Rehe, which is the duty of soldiers. We worked hard for the country, and the soldiers were determined to die to resist and kill the enemy. However, we were an isolated army outside the Great Wall, and our rear was cut off, so we could not fight for long. When we retreated from Chifeng to Cone Mountain, we held our ground and planned to connect with friendly forces to attack Chengde's rear, but we were separated by thousands of miles and could not coordinate. Now that the war has ended, our army has witnessed the difficulties of the country. We will never participate in civil wars again and will concentrate on training to serve the country in the future. We are now ordered to move west, but the roads are rugged, and the population is sparse. Without sufficient preparation, long-distance marching will be difficult. The uniforms, shoes, socks, and all supplies that we have made could not be delivered earlier due to the situation in Chahar, but they will be delivered within days. Currently, in addition to strict training, our army is also repairing roads and preparing to drill wells in waterless areas along the way to be prepared when we depart in the future. However, it is now autumn, and the weather is getting colder. If we delay another month, we will not be able to depart. If we cannot depart this year, our original intention will not change. As long as there is an order, we will still move west at any time."

In addition to Sun's troops, there is also Wang Jingguo's 70th Division stationed in Baotou. Most of the troops are stationed outside the city, and there are few troops stationed inside the city. The military and civilians live in harmony, and the area is peaceful.

Baotou is the terminal of the Ping Sui Railway and the gathering place for goods from the Northwest. It was quite prosperous in 1926 and 1927, with a population of about 180,000. Goods from the Northwest were loaded and unloaded here for transport to the East. In recent years, it has declined, and the population has decreased to less than 100,000. Trade and transportation have also stagnated. The main reasons are the heavy taxes and the inconvenient transportation. There are as many as sixteen or seventeen tax collection agencies in Baotou. Goods are heavily taxed upon arrival, making them impossible to sell, which discourages merchants. Opium from Gansu and Qinghai is exported in large quantities every year and used to be transshipped through Baotou. In recent years, it is transported directly from Shaanxi to the East without the need for travel. As for the local products of fur and wool, they are all stagnant, and prices have fallen. No one is collecting or transporting them. If this continues, the future will be very dangerous.

The city walls of Baotou are made of earth, and most of the houses are also earthen houses. The streets and alleys are all dirt roads, with sand up to the shins. On sunny days, red dust fills the air. When the wind blows, sand and rocks fly. After heavy rain, it becomes muddy and difficult to travel. In addition, sanitation is neglected, and flies and mosquitoes abound. It is a typical Northwestern city, and there is still a long way to go in terms of improvement. (August 21st)

Completion of Four Major Provincial Highways in Jiangxi 94

Yu Ping Railway Surveying is About to be Completed

Headquarters Orders Bandit Suppression Troops to Rush to Build Highways

Nanchang Correspondence: In Jiangxi Province, where bandits are everywhere and specialize in disrupting transportation, the authorities are still actively implementing road construction projects. According to recent investigations, the four major provincial highways have been completed in succession. The situation is as follows:

Jiangxi-Hunan Highway 95

The entire route can be completed within this month. Starting from the 20th, it can be reached from the provincial capital directly to Pingxiang by car in eight hours. It can also be connected from Pingxiang to the Zhuping Road and then to the Yuehan Road. A new era of transportation has been opened in the rugged mountains of western Jiangxi.

Jiangxi-Zhejiang Highway 96

This route was originally scheduled to be completed last year. However, the section of Yanshan, Yiyang, and Guixi was severely damaged by Fang Zhimin's bandit group. It was destroyed and rebuilt, and rebuilt and destroyed again. As a result, it is now fully completed. Tickets will be sold for the direct Nanchang to Yushan route starting from the first of next month. The opening ceremony will be held in Hekou on that day. There is currently a motor road from Yushan to Changshan. In the future, it will be connected to the Hangjiang Road, so Nanchang can use this route to reach the sea.

Jiangxi-Fujian Highway 97

This route has long been open to Nancheng, and a branch line is also open to Nanfeng. However, the section from Nancheng to Lichuan, which directly reaches the Fujian border, is still missing. Now that Lichuan has been recovered, the highway office is preparing to advance with the army to complete this section to reach Guangze in Fujian.

Jiangxi-Guangdong Line 98

The northern section of this line has long been open to Majiazhou in Taihe. The southern section, built by the Guangdong army, can reach Dayu from Nanxiong. There are still several sections in Taihe, Ganxian, and Nankang, which have been severely affected by bandits. No one can be assigned to work. Now Chairman Chiang has negotiated with the National Economic Council to allocate 100,000 yuan to the Southern Route Headquarters and the Jiangxi Provincial Government to carry out the project in sections to open up the Jiangxi-Guangdong transportation to facilitate the bandit suppression military in Ganjiang. It is expected that the completion date will not be far away.

The Yuping Railway is the only important east-west route in the Southeast, and it is extremely important for both defense and economy. The surveying team sent by the railway is currently rushing to survey and can be completed as scheduled. The provincial government believes that the engineering costs borne by the province are in urgent need of funds (the cost of railway track materials is borne by the central government), and has decided to use the salt surcharge as a fund to issue public bonds of 12 million yuan to complete the project as soon as possible. After this road is completed, it can be connected to the Yuehan, Hangjiang and other routes, and the products of the southeastern provinces can be shipped out of the Zhapu estuary.

Chairman Chiang believes that transportation is the only key to clearing bandits, so he has repeatedly ordered the provinces of Jiangxi, Guangdong, Fujian, Hunan, and Hubei to quickly complete the roads in the bandit areas, and stipulated that each division of the garrison must build 50 kilometers of roads in the defense zone every month, except during combat. The headquarters will subsidize 100 yuan per kilometer, and 200 yuan for those who pave stones. At present, the border roads of Jiangxi-Hubei, Jiangxi-Hunan, and Jiangxi-Guangdong are all presided over by the garrison troops, and the construction is being stepped up. Remote areas will soon see connectivity in all directions. (August 24th)

Ministry of Finance Trials

Anqing Bulk Salt Transportation 99

The Datong Chamber of Commerce Asks to Preserve the Salt Wharf

Anqing Correspondence: Datong Town, which belongs to Tongling County in Anhui Province, was only a small barren island before the Xianfeng period of the Qing Dynasty. During the Hongyang Rebellion, people from various prefectures of Huizhou and Ningguo came here to seek refuge, and houses were built one after another, forming a settlement. In the second year of the Tongzhi reign, the General Bureau for the Supervision and Sale of Huai Salt was established in this area (renamed the Anhui Wharf Revenue Transport Bureau in the Republic of China) to recruit merchants to transport Huainan salt, build warehouses for storage, and sell it in the eleven counties of Tongling, Qingyang, Guichi, Shitai, Zhizhi, Huaining, Qianshan, Taihu, Wangjiang, and Susong. Those who went to Datong to purchase salt from various counties also loaded local products for barter, so that the area and the opposite bank of Heyuezhou (now both banks are collectively referred to as Datong) have become an important commercial port in southern Anhui over the decades, almost competing with the provincial city of Wuhu. Recently, the Ministry of Finance, according to the telegram from the Huaibei Branch of the Salt Affairs Inspection General Office, stated that, in order to promote the rotation of the Anqing shipping, the wharf (referring to Datong, i.e., the Anhui wharf) has not transported or sold a grain of Huai salt in recent years, which is almost equivalent to an abandoned wharf. In order to open up the abandoned wharf and promote Huai salt, it is necessary to first transport cheap and high-quality salt from Huaibei in order to compete for sales. Moreover, the introduction of the southern Anhui salt is controlled by a small number of people, and the rent price is surprisingly high, making it impossible for other merchants to transport salt. There is a tendency to abandon the wharf rather than allow other merchants to transport salt. It is now proposed to carry out a pilot rotation of salt (Datong has always relied on sailing vessels) with 100 tickets, i.e., 96,000 dan, with the introduction of the northern and southern Anhui salt, and the salt pounds will be allocated to Jinan and Huaibei, each transporting half, and first transport the high-quality salt from Huaibei to open its way. Once it has been successfully operated and the situation of the arrival and competitive sale of the two salts of Jinan and Huaibei has been examined, the permanent quota will be determined. It is heard that the Ministry of Finance has approved the request and has ordered the two Huai transport envoys, the Huainan transport deputy, and the Anhui Wharf Revenue Transport Bureau to inform them. However, the Datong Chamber of Commerce and other organizations believe that the commercial port has always relied on salt transport as its main source of income. If this case is realized, the market will plummet, which will have a huge impact. Therefore, a joint association of all sectors was organized to preserve the Huainan wharf and to relieve the market and people's livelihood. A meeting was held to express opposition, and four representatives, Fang Duancheng, Sun Faxu, Hu Chaorong, and Li Ziyuan, were sent to the province yesterday to petition various parties. They have already submitted a petition to the provincial government, explaining various reasons and requesting that they be forwarded to the Ministry of Finance to withdraw the order. The representatives also plan to go to Beijing within days to appeal to the Ministry of Finance again to achieve the goal of cancellation. (August 26th)

Songjiang 100

Strict Prohibition of Setting off Firecrackers in the Urban Area 101

Jiang Yunqing, Battalion Commander of the Second Battalion of the Third Security Regiment, stated that the setting off of firecrackers in the urban area day and night often caused confusion with the sound of guns and cannons, causing misunderstandings from time to time. If a bandit alarm occurred, it would lead to failure. He was preparing to take measures to reduce it when he received instructions from the Provincial Government through the Security Office to strictly prohibit the setting off of firecrackers. He then sent a letter to the county to forward it to the Public Security Bureau and the First District Office to implement it. A notice was posted, but the custom in Songjiang was deeply rooted and difficult to eradicate at once. On the 28th, during a meeting of township chiefs convened by the First District Office, Commissioner Jin and Battalion Commander Jiang personally gave instructions, explaining that the township chiefs must instruct the village police and neighborhood chiefs to inform each household that the setting off of firecrackers is strictly prohibited day and night. If it occurs, the village police and neighborhood chiefs must investigate and hand them over. Otherwise, if it is found that they have not reported it, the village police and neighborhood chiefs will be held jointly responsible. Starting tomorrow, gongs will be used to warn each section, and strict inspections will be carried out starting from September 3rd.

Gaoyou

Provincial Committee Thoroughly Investigates Party Affairs Disputes 102

More than 30 party members in this county, including Jia Yuqiang, had been studying or working in Shanghai and returned to their hometowns during the summer vacation this year, intending to transfer their party membership back. However, the members of the county party committee, fearing that the re-election would fail, refused to transfer them. Jia and others were angry at the committee's control of party affairs and filed a complaint with the provincial party headquarters. It is now heard that the province has appointed Li Junliang to Gaoyou to thoroughly investigate.

Nantong

Two Bandits in Tongzhou and Rugao Sentenced to Death 103

Tao Dongyan, a notorious bandit in Tongzhou and Rugao counties, was captured in Pingchao. During the interrogation at the county government, he confessed to robbery, arson, and murder without hesitation. The victims also appeared in court to testify. County Magistrate Ye has sentenced the two bandits to death and telegraphed the provincial government for approval to execute them.

Zhenjiang

Police and Bandits Fight in the Southern Suburbs 104

Yesterday, the Provincial Public Security Bureau's Detective Team received a report from Detective Wang Juru that a bandit gang led by Zhang Huoyuan was entrenched in Shantian, Baigang Village in the southern suburbs, and was hiding hostages. Captain Shao, acting on the report, ordered Detectives Li Xingwu, Zhang Xiuzhi, and Ma Buyun to lead a dozen detectives in disguise at 10 p.m. that night. They arrived at the bandit den in the dead of night. The village dogs barked wildly. The bandits, hearing the alarm, came out to investigate and realized that they were being apprehended by detectives. More than 30 bandits fired box cannons and fought with Detective Li and others. Detectives Li, Zhang, and Ma and other detectives bravely charged forward. After two hours of fighting, the bandits were overwhelmed and retreated. As a result, four bandits, including Ye Xiufu (aka Dagouzi), Zhu Dazuo, Xia Zhaolu, and Xia Fucai, were captured. Two box cannons, 30 bullets, and two hostages, Zang Xufu, a seven-year-old child from Danyang, and Chen Gensan, were seized. During the firefight, cannonballs were dense like beads. Detective Wang Juru, who bravely fought at the forefront, was shot and killed on the spot. The detectives carried his body back and temporarily placed it in the Taiping Temple on Xinma Road. Detective Li and others led the captured four bandits and hostages back to report. The suspects are currently under investigation.

Xiaoshan

Cargo Ship Capsizes, Drowning Five People 105

On the morning of the 27th, a cargo ship coming from Shangjiang capsized at Dongjiangzui in Xiaoshan due to the impact of the tide. All the paper goods and sundries sank to the bottom of the river. Five of the twelve passengers and boatmen drowned. Most tragically, a ten-year-old child was trapped in the cabin and drowned because the bottom of the boat was facing up and could not be rescued in time.

Daughter-in-Law Flees, Son Dies, Mother Commits Suicide 106

Qu Zonghai, a resident of the western suburbs of Xiaoshan, had been working as a partner in a sock factory in Shanghai. He returned home last month due to illness. His wife, Yu, had been having an affair. Her husband returned home sick, and the family was in financial straits. On the 25th, she secretly fled. Qu, bedridden, received this news and hanged himself at midnight. Unexpectedly, his 70-year-old mother was also at home. Because her daughter-in-law had fled and her son had died, she had no means of living and drowned in the Qiantang River on the 27th. Of the five members of the family, only two daughters remain. How tragic!

Today's Welcome for Minister Song's Return to China 107

Eurasia Aviation Sends Plane to Shanghai to Greet Him

Citywide Stores to Fly Flags Today in Celebration

Government and Business Leaders from Nanjing and Shanghai to Welcome Him in the Early Morning

Chinese and Foreign Police Forces to Provide Tight Security

Song Ziwen, Vice President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, was ordered to go to Washington to attend President Roosevelt's World Economic Conference, and to London to attend the World Economic Conference. He also traveled to the United States, Germany, France, and Italy. He returned to China on the 13th aboard the Dollar Steamship Company's President Jefferson from Seattle. He is expected to arrive in Shanghai this morning at 10 a.m. Various sectors have made preparations for a warm welcome. After arriving in Shanghai, Song will go to Nanjing and Lushan to report on the trip. The details are as follows:

Tight Security Expected to Arrive at 10 a.m.

According to news from the Dollar Steamship Company yesterday, the President Jefferson set sail from Kobe the day before yesterday and is expected to arrive at Wusongkou at 5:30 a.m. today. However, the weather was rainy yesterday and the wind and waves along the way were strong, so the ship's speed was slower and is expected to arrive at the Bailianjing Dollar Wharf in Pudong at 10 a.m. today. The municipal government expects a large number of people to welcome him, including key figures from the party and the country. Yesterday, it specially ordered Yang Hu, Director of the Municipal Security Bureau, and Wen Hongen, Director of the Public Security Bureau, and notified the public security authorities in the concession to provide tight security. It is reported that the Security Bureau and the Public Security Bureau will send a large security team, a large police team, and a large water patrol team to patrol and guard the area around the Sixteen Pups and the Bailianjing Wharf in Pudong. Detective Captain Lu Ying will also send armed detectives to provide close protection on the spot. It is also reported that the Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement and the French Concession Police Department will also send a large number of Chinese and foreign detectives to protect the area around the Customs Wharf and the junction of the French Concession. The municipal government has cleared a space behind the Dada Company in Nanshi as a parking area for guests and has decided to temporarily close the traffic from Xiaodongmen Road to Guanqiao from 6:30 a.m. today until Song lands and passes by. A sign has been posted at the entrance of Dada Wharf No. 5, Xiaodongmen, stating "Welcome Minister Song, a pass is required to enter" to limit access. Three ceremonial arches have been erected at Dada Wharf to show respect.

After Minister Song arrives in Shanghai, he will immediately go to Nanjing to report to the central government on the process of this trip, and go to Lushan to meet Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. President Wang Jingwei originally intended to come to Shanghai in person to welcome him, but due to busy political affairs in Nanjing, he was unable to spare time. Weary from Travel, Outstanding Service 113

Finance Minister Song left Shanghai on April 18th to go abroad, arrived in Seattle on May 2nd, and then safely arrived in Washington D.C. on the 6th via Chicago. U.S. Secretary of State Hull personally went to the station to welcome him. On the 6th, he was accompanied by Chinese Ambassador to the U.S. Shi Zhaoji to the White House to formally meet President Roosevelt. At noon on the 8th, President Roosevelt hosted a banquet for Finance Minister Song. After the banquet, they began talks to discuss various issues. Secretary of State Hull also hosted a banquet for Finance Minister Song on the 10th and continued talks, paying particular attention to the silver issue. After several discussions, a $50 million U.S. dollar loan for American cotton and wheat was established. Finance Minister Song then left Washington on the 19th for New York. On June 5th, via Southampton, together with Yan Huiqing and Gu Weijun, he went to London, the capital of England, to attend the World Economic Conference. The conference opened on the 12th. Finance Minister Song specially visited British Prime Minister MacDonald the day before to discuss everything. When the conference opened, China proposed the issue of stabilizing silver prices and requested the establishment of a small committee to discuss the silver issue. On July 22nd, China, India, Spain, Australia, Bolivia, Canada, Mexico, Peru, and the United States signed a four-year silver agreement in London, stipulating that it would take effect from January 1, 1934. Finance Minister Song took the opportunity of the adjournment of the economic conference on June 20th to go to Paris to meet with French Foreign Minister Pongu. On the 21st, he met with French Prime Minister Daladier to discuss the Far East issue. On the 22nd, he quickly returned to London. On July 1st, he had an audience with the King of England. On the 11th, he went to Rome to visit Italian Prime Minister Mussolini. The Italian Prime Minister, on behalf of the King of Italy, presented the Finance Minister with the Cross Medal. The League of Nations' Chinese Technical Cooperation Committee held a meeting in Paris on the 18th, and Finance Minister Song quickly went to Paris again, accompanied by Ambassador Gu Weijun to attend. Finance Minister Song expressed that China urgently needed League of Nations technical personnel to assist in China's construction efforts. The committee then appointed Dr. Rajchman, Director of the Health Section, to come to China as a liaison to preside over this work. Finance Minister Song then went to Belgium on the 19th, visited Belgian Foreign Minister Hymans, and had an audience with the King of Belgium. On the 21st, he left Belgium for Germany, staying in Berlin for a week, visiting German authorities and leaders of the industrial and commercial sectors. On the 27th, he returned to Paris and met with Zhang Xueliang. The next day, he had an audience with the President of France. The French President personally awarded Finance Minister Song the Grand Cross of the Legion of Honor. On the 29th, he left France for the United States. President Roosevelt met with Finance Minister Song again at Hyde Park on August 7th and talked at length about the Far East issue. On the 13th, he turned back to Seattle and boarded a ship to return home. Finance Minister Song traveled tirelessly and ran around Europe and America, working hard for the country. His achievements are very great. The American cotton and wheat loan, the silver agreement, and the increase in League of Nations technical cooperation are all great gains from Finance Minister Song's trip. In addition, his diplomatic skills, revealing the truth about the Far East, and promoting the glory of the Chinese nation are all praised by the people of the country.

Visited Mayor Wu Yesterday 119

Declared the Purpose of the Anti-War Conference

Sir Malet, the British representative and chairman of the Far East Conference of the World Anti-War Alliance, after being refused entry by Japan and returning to Shanghai, visited Mr. Peel, the Director-General, and Mr. Fessenden, the Director, of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession. Yesterday (August 28th) at 12 noon, he went to the Municipal Government to visit Mayor Wu, who received him. It is reported that Sir Malet, in addition to the visit, also inquired about the Municipal Government's attitude towards the Anti-War Conference. Mayor Wu said that China has always valued peace, and no one opposes the purpose of anti-war. However, he has recently received reports from various parties that the Communist Party in Shanghai is attempting to use the opportunity of the Anti-War Conference to carry out its own activities. We cannot currently determine whether the Third International has actual control over the Anti-War Conference. Furthermore, Shanghai suffered significant losses after the war and urgently needs to restore its pre-war state. It cannot withstand further social unrest. Therefore, the Municipal Government's sole responsibility is to maintain local security and protect the peaceful life and order of the people. Sir Malet also deeply agreed, and at the same time stated that the Anti-War Conference is not controlled by the Third International. If the Communist Party takes the opportunity to carry out activities, the conference can be immediately closed to clarify its attitude. After the discussion, he left. It is reported that Sir Malet still hopes to choose a suitable location in the Public Concession or the French Concession to hold the conference. However, because the American representative has not yet arrived in Shanghai, it is still pending.

Labor Strike at British-American Tobacco Factory

Both Sides are Insisting 123

The Completion Case Has Been Submitted to Arbitration, the School Case Will Be Mediated Today

The Fifth District Labor Union Held an Emergency Meeting at 5 PM Yesterday

Eight thousand workers from the new and old British-American Tobacco factories in Pudong have been on strike since the 25th due to the factory's failure to resolve the outstanding labor-management disputes, resulting in a complete standstill of all work. On the day before yesterday, the weekly holiday, the workers did not go to the factory. The female workers of the new factory, after being refused entry by the factory, have been allowed to enter the factory after negotiations.

The Labor Union Submitted a Document to the Fifth District Cigarette Workers Union, submitting to the Social Affairs Bureau to continue to revise the labor-management mutual aid conditions. The original document stated, "Submitting for approval, the conditions for labor-management mutual aid that the union and the factory signed in 1927 are mostly inconsistent with the facts or lower than the current treatment. We have previously submitted a request for appropriate amendments to maintain treatment, and have been summoned for mediation. However, the union's case has been delayed for a long time and is still stagnant. Now that it is the autumn of labor-management affairs, the factory is arbitrarily destroying the conditions. It is difficult to delay the amendment for a long time. Therefore, we submit to your bureau to immediately continue to convene mediation to maintain treatment and bring the matter to an end. Respectfully submitted."

Submitted to Arbitration, the Social Affairs Bureau Instructed the Fifth District Cigarette Workers Union, "For knowledge, in the case of the factory's reduction of work dispute, because mediation failed, the entire file was sent to the government to apply for arbitration. Previously, we received the Municipal Government's No. 7165 instruction stating, 'All documents are noted, and permission is granted to submit to arbitration.' You should know, this order, the file is temporarily stored, etc. Having received this, in addition to the separate order, we hereby order you to know. This order, August 26, 1933, Wu Xingya, Director of the Bureau."

Mediation Today Regarding labor and education matters, the Social Affairs Bureau is scheduled to convene mediation today. The day before yesterday, the union was instructed, "For compliance, in the dispute between the company's labor and management over the workers' children's school, the bureau, together with the Education Bureau and the Municipal Party Department, sent personnel to mediate. A consensus was generally reached, but there are still several unresolved points. After submitting the case to the government for instructions, we received the Municipal Government's No. 7062 instruction stating, 'All documents are noted.

The six unresolved points in the case have been separately reviewed and approved by the government as follows: (omitted) This order, the original file is returned, etc. Having received this, in addition to the separate notification, we hereby order you to comply and send two responsible representatives to the bureau at 2 PM on the 29th of this month to attend the mediation on time, without delay. This order, August 26, 1933, Wu Xingya, Director of the Bureau."

Emergency Meeting The Fifth District Cigarette Workers Union held an emergency meeting at its Pudong office at 5:20 PM yesterday to discuss countermeasures. Approximately 150 representatives from various departments attended, with Chen Peide, Liu Dehua, and Lou Jingguan serving as the presidium. Lu Yinchu was sent by the Municipal Party Department to attend and provide guidance. Chairman Chen Peide first reported on the negotiation process of various cases and the subsequent countermeasures.

Passed Various Motions (1) Whether to organize a strike committee, Resolved: Passed. Decided on 39 members (20 members of the union's board of directors and supervisors, and 19 temporary nominees, jointly forming the committee). (2) Issue a notice to workers, Resolved: Passed. (3) This month's membership fee, Resolved: To be collected starting on the 30th. (4) Invite the press tomorrow and schedule a banquet for all sectors to request assistance, Resolved: Passed. (5) Workers are not allowed to leave the factory during the strike period after entering the factory until quitting time, Resolved: Passed. (6) Wages during the strike period shall be paid by the factory at the normal rate, Resolved: Passed. Wu Huanzhang talks.

Post-Affairs Measures of the Ma Department in Chahar Province 124

Ma Zhanshan and Huang Fu Agreed in Moganshan

Deng Wen's Successor Was Officially Recommended by Ma

Yesterday morning, a reporter from the New Voice News Agency met with Mr. Wu Huanzhang, Ma Zhanshan's representative, and asked about the content of Chairman Huang's meeting with Mr. Ma. According to him, Chairman Huang and Chairman Ma met for three hours, and the focus of the discussions was on two points: (1) The Ma Department in Chahar Province currently has 10,000 people. After discussion, it was agreed to transfer the department directly to the Beiping Military Branch Council, and the military pay will also be allocated monthly by the Military Branch Council. The location of the garrison will also be designated by the Military Branch Council soon, and the official relocation will take place at a determined location. (2) Regarding the resettlement of the old department, in addition to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's order to submit the names of all civil and military subordinates, it has been agreed to have the central government arrange for the resettlement of the old Heilongjiang provincial government officials and assign them to various positions, and the military officers will be assigned to various armies by Chairman Chiang. However, during the conversation with Chairman Huang, Mr. Huang also agreed to arrange for a portion to be placed in the Beiping Political Branch Council. As for the selection of a successor after the death of Division Commander Deng Wen, Chairman Chiang has ordered Ma Wenxi to recommend one of Ma's Chief of Staff Rong Yusu and the two who have been temporarily acting without authorization for the committee member to choose. Chairman Chiang, in view of Deng Wen's contribution to resolving the Chahar situation this time, will request the central government to provide generous compensation for Deng Wen's tragic death.

Dr. Millikan Tests Cosmic Rays 125

Can Launch Tiny Bullets

Shoot at World Liners

The Great American Evening News says, "Today (28th), the President Garfield of the Dollar Steamship Lines, which arrived in Shanghai, was often shot at by bullets during its voyage, but these bullets were infinitely small and not fired from guns, but came from strange cosmic rays. This light often bombards the earth from distant space. Although the President Garfield is not its special target, it is noteworthy that the famous physicist Dr. Millikan of the California Institute of Technology had installed a very accurate cosmic ray detector on board, which can measure the intensity and quantity of cosmic rays. When the ship sails around the world, it can use the device to measure the effect of cosmic rays in different latitudes and longitudes, and continuously record them on film. This instrument is very simple to manufacture. It only uses a six-inch diameter steel ball, filled with atmospheric gas under 60 pounds of pressure per square inch, and an ordinary electroscope, which is charged by a battery at regular intervals. When cosmic rays penetrate the steel shell, like X-rays (i.e., X-rays) passing through the human body, this light can cause argon atoms to explode, ionize, and then cause electrical effects, causing the electroscope to partially discharge. Then, by looking at the rate of discharge, the index of the amount of cosmic rays in the area can be measured. Dr. Millikan will continuously capture these phenomena on film that is constantly running, creating a record. The film is very long and can run for four months around the earth. It not only records the movement of the electroscope, but also simultaneously records the temperature, atmospheric pressure, and time. Outside the steel ball, it is lined with a four-hour thick lead box to prevent interference from nearby radioactive substances, because cosmic rays are never hindered by lead, unlike other radioactive rays. Regarding the nature of cosmic rays, scientists are still exploring them. It is only known that they have very high transmittance and extremely high electrical potential, about more than 300 million electron volts, which is nearly a thousand times higher than other known radioactive rays on earth, such as X-rays and meson rays. Therefore, studying these extremely small and terrifying destructive bullets is an extremely important task in the scientific community today."

Mayor Wu Speaks

Maintaining Public Security and Serving Morality 131

Yesterday Morning at the Municipal Government Memorial Week

According to the Central News Agency, the Municipal Government held a memorial week for the Prime Minister yesterday morning. Over 300 employees from the Municipal Government and various bureaus attended. Mayor Wu Tiecheng presided over the ceremony and reported on "Maintaining Public Security and Serving Morality." The main points are as follows:

Devote Oneself to Duty 132

Fellow Comrades, the Prime Minister told us,

If we want to revive the Chinese nation, we must first restore our self-confidence and the inherent morality of China. Morality is the basic creed of our lives, and self-confidence is the key to our success in doing things. Where is the principle of our lives? First, we must have ambition and aspirations. Second, we must be devoted to our duties, which is to fulfill our responsibilities. Whether we are serving in an administrative agency as a civil servant, serving in the business community, or operating our own business, if everyone can be devoted to their duties and make their business successful, there must be a kind of ambition, a kind of self-confidence. In other words, if the people of the whole country, regardless of whether they are scholars, farmers, workers, merchants, soldiers, or politicians, can have this kind of ambition, this kind of aspiration, to be devoted to the duties and careers they are engaged in, I believe they will definitely succeed.

Mourning Ma and Huang 133

The reason why I want to say this today

is that in the past two years, comrades in the Public Safety Bureau who have been handling special affairs have repeatedly been killed by enemies because of their duties. Many have sacrificed their lives. The most prominent are Comrade Ma Shaowu and Comrade Huang Yonghua, who was recently killed. These comrades who sacrificed for their devotion to duty, because they only knew where their responsibilities lay, regardless of all interests, had the ambition and aspirations to serve the society and devote themselves to their respective duties, and finally sacrificed their lives. The sacrifice of such brave, responsible, and devoted comrades is a great loss to us, and at the same time, it can serve as a good example for a group of people, especially those of us who are civil servants. Since we are going to serve the people, we should continue their spirit of devotion to duty and courage to sacrifice, and devote ourselves

to our duties and complete our careers.

Encourage Subordinates 134

Shanghai, in the past one or two years, in the midst of this national crisis, and at the same time, the society is so complex, with many dangerous elements lurking, undermining the law and disrupting public security. They are not only plotting and destroying the peaceful order of society, creating an atmosphere of terror and unease in society, but also taking the opportunity to stir up trouble, wanting to subvert the government. Shanghai, on the one hand, is in a time of national crisis, and on the other hand, it is in such a complex and serious social situation. The maintenance of its public security should be very difficult in theory. However, the public security of Shanghai, the peaceful order of the whole territory, is not only the same as before the September 18th Incident, but also the social disputes are less than before. This fact is obvious to all and recognized by the society. Why is Shanghai able to be so stable? There are two reasons. First, the citizens of Shanghai all know the importance of Shanghai's position, and at the same time know that the safety of Shanghai is closely related to the safety of the nation. The citizens of Shanghai have this understanding and work together with the strength of the citizens of Shanghai to stabilize Shanghai. The citizens of Shanghai have this understanding and this effort, so Shanghai can be stable. This is the first reason. Second, the dangerous elements of Shanghai's reactionaries are being eliminated day by day, and the dens of conspiracy in Shanghai are being cracked down on day by day. The dangerous reactionary elements of Shanghai can be eliminated day by day, and the dens of conspiracy can be cracked down on day by day. We cannot but attribute this to the comrades in the Public Safety Bureau who are able to be devoted to their duties, and to the cooperation between the public concession, the French concession police, and the Public Safety Bureau, so that the public security of Shanghai can be maintained. This is the second reason. Because of these two reasons, Shanghai can have such stability. Here, we cannot but express our respect and condolences to the comrades who sacrificed for maintaining the peace and security of Shanghai. All these words I say today are to encourage all the staff of the Shanghai Municipal Government, and at the same time to encourage myself.

Huang Naishu Talks About Retired Postal Workers 135

A Total of 200,000 Yuan in Pensions and Other Payments Were Issued

Approximately 100,000 Yuan Will Be Saved in Salaries Each Year Thereafter

Huang Naishu, Director-General of the Postal Administration, told a reporter from the Central News Agency that the bureau had laid off 32 employees to save money, which was originally done in accordance with the regulations. Unexpectedly, it caused misunderstandings among the employees and was opposed. Finally, with the Ministry of Communications' flexible method, the layoffs were changed to voluntary retirement, and two months' salary was given in addition to severance, and the issue was resolved. However, the employees said that the occurrence of the dispute was due to my tough attitude. In fact, the bureau is an executive agency, and everything must be done in accordance with the regulations. Even if there is a need for flexibility, it must be approved by the ministry. Therefore, my inability to change the method without authorization is also my responsibility, and not a desire to insist on my personal opinions, so as to make the situation deadlocked. This time, the retired employees include 8 from the Shanghai Bureau, 8 from the Fuzhou Bureau, 4 from the Nanjing Bureau, and one or two from other bureaus, a total of 32 people. A total of about 200,000 yuan will be issued for pensions and two months' salary. Approximately 100,000 yuan can be saved in salaries each year thereafter.

Special Tax on Domestic Tobacco

Supplements Approved to Show Flexibility 137

Ministry of Finance Tax Affairs Department Replies to Chamber of Commerce

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, previously based on a letter from the Jiujiang Transfer Industry Association, requested that the special tax on domestic tobacco be levied in different grades, and forwarded it to the Tax Affairs Department of the Ministry of Finance. Yesterday, the Tax Affairs Department of the Ministry of Finance replied, "I have received the telegram from Jian. I have checked the previous report from the Jiujiang Special Tax Office for Domestic Tobacco, which was based on a letter from the Jiujiang Transfer Industry Association, requesting that the special tax on domestic tobacco be levied in different grades, and that existing inventory be exempted from the new tax. The Tax Affairs Department previously stated that the Susong Tobacco Industry Association and others jointly sent a telegram requesting that the newly established special tax rate for domestic tobacco leaves be supplemented by exceptions to alleviate the difficulties of merchants. The Ministry of Finance stated that the cancellation of the public sales fees and taxes on domestic tobacco leaves in the seven provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Henan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Fujian was changed to a special tax in order to simplify the process and facilitate merchants. The established special tax rate of 4.15 yuan per 100 market liters is no more than a combination of the previously levied public sales fees and taxes, unified collection, and once a collection is sufficient, it can be sold at will within the special tax area without re-collection, and the customs transit tax is also approved for exemption. The Ministry has promulgated the Provisional Regulations for the Collection of Special Taxes on Domestic Tobacco Leaves, and ordered the competent bureaus in each province to comply with them uniformly from July 1 of this year. Compared with the previous public sales fees and taxes, which were based on provinces, if tobacco leaves were transported from the place of production and sale to other provinces, they would still have to be taxed at the place of sale. The convenience to tobacco merchants is very obvious. How can the merchants misunderstand and suddenly want to change the tax regulations based on the special circumstances of tobacco leaf production and sales in a corner of the country?" The office was ordered to inform them. The Jiujiang Transfer Industry Association requested that the special tax on domestic tobacco leaves be levied in different grades.

The review is consistent and should be interpreted and informed by the office in accordance with the case. Regarding the methods for paying the new tax and refunding the old tax on inventory after the implementation of the special tax on domestic tobacco leaves issued by the department, the Shanghai Tobacco Leaf Industry Association previously stated the difficulties, and the department immediately reviewed and approved various supplementary points to show flexibility and ordered the association to inform them and distributed them to various bureaus for reference. If the original method is

indeed difficult to implement, the office should quickly assess the situation and refer to the supplementary points approved by the department to facilitate the procedures and submit them to the department for approval and implementation to comply with the wishes of the merchants. The office was ordered to comply. Now that the association has resubmitted the previous situation, it should be approved in accordance with the case and ordered to inform them. This approval.

Box Corpse Case

Portuguese Consul Summons Witnesses This Morning 140

Investigating Whether the Murderer's Brother Was an Accomplice

After Questioning, the Murderer Will Be Sent to Macau

Since the principal offender in the box corpse case, Balie, confessed to killing the Cantonese woman Zhang Cailian last Saturday, the entire case has been largely determined. Yesterday, the Portuguese Consul stated that Qiu Shifu, who assisted in transporting the body, had not yet confessed to being an accomplice, so another trial was required. Currently, the Portuguese Consul has collected reliable evidence from witnesses, such as the Japanese man Ozo, the Japanese woman Chie, residents of No. 14 Jiaxing Road, and Ma Xiaowei, an employee of a box shop on Broadway Road, regarding the purchase of the box, which is sufficient to prove Qiu Shifu's assistance in moving the body. According to Ma Xiaowei's testimony, at 8:00 AM on the 5th, a person came to buy a box and paid a deposit of one yuan. When he came to pick up the box at 11:00 AM, two people came together, indicating that Qiu Shifu also went. For fear that the foreigners would cause him trouble or retaliate in the future, he did not dare to identify him in court. The Portuguese Consul stated that regarding the issue of whether or not the accomplice was guilty, since he was trying to deny it, it was necessary for the witnesses to prove it. Otherwise, according to Portuguese law, the interrogation must be clear within 24 hours, otherwise, the person cannot be detained. Therefore, this morning, the Portuguese Consulate may summon the witnesses to re-examine whether the accomplice was present, whether he participated in moving the body, and whether he was an accomplice. After this inquiry is clarified, the criminals will be scheduled to be sent to Macau.

Autopsy of Beggar's Corpse 141

Determined That Gu Kou Died of Illness

Gu Xiaomei and Others Interrogated

Gu Xiaomei, a native of Tongzhou, is 64 years old. His cousin, Gu Kou, is also in his sixties. Both of them make a living by begging in Shanghai, seeking alms from door to door to make a living. On the morning of the 21st of this month, at 11:00 AM, Gu Kou, accompanied by a beggar named Zhengming, begged to No. 142 Lan Road, in front of the Yongtai Xiang Cigarette and Paper Shop. Just as he was about to stop to ask for alms, he suddenly suffered an acute illness and collapsed, unconscious. He was immediately sent by the No. 6 Gang Police to the Sacred Heart Hospital for treatment, but he died before treatment could be provided. After investigation by the Yangshupu Police Station, it was confirmed that he was a beggar who died on the road, so the Pushan Villa was notified to prepare a coffin for collection and temporary placement. After three days, Gu Xiaomei, based on what the beggar Zhengming said, that Gu Kou was beaten to death by the owner of the Yongtai Xiang shop, deeply believed it and reported it to the police station, requesting a thorough investigation. The police chief did not pay attention to it because it had already been clarified at the time. Gu Xiaomei was not satisfied and submitted a petition to the Prosecutor's Office of the First Special District Court, requesting an autopsy. It has been approved and the police station has been notified to transport the coffin to the Phelon Road Autopsy Office to await a forensic examination in accordance with the law, and a report will be submitted for review. It is now understood that Gu Kou's remains were examined in detail by a forensic doctor yesterday, and the result was determined to be death from illness, with no other circumstances. An autopsy report was issued and sent to the Prosecutor's Office. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo Wei went to the Autopsy Office and ordered the police station to summon Gu Xiaomei and Zhengming for interrogation. The police chief submitted the Sacred Heart Hospital's diagnosis certificate for Gu Kou's diagnosis on that day, stating that the hospital had determined that the deceased was ill. Gu Xiaomei and Zhengming insisted on pointing to being beaten after the collection. Their actions had no other purpose, or they hoped to use it as an excuse for blackmail. In order to understand the content, the police station planned to investigate Gu Xiaomei and Zhengming. Prosecutor Guo Wei then ordered the Pushan Villa to handle the coffin because the body had been examined and determined to be dead from illness. The two beggars, Gu Xiaomei and others, were taken to the Yangshupu Police Station for questioning.

Rent Books and Sublease Books Must Be Stamped

Jiangsu Shangbao Stamp Tax Branch Proclamation No. 13 states, "For the purpose of proclamation, according to the Stamp Tax Regulations, all leased land should be affixed with stamps as legal proof. It is now found that the two types of rent books and sublease books issued by the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau are for landlords in the urban area to report to the police district to which they are assigned to tenants and sublessors when they lease a house, which is an official rent receipt and should be in accordance with Article 2, Category 1, Item 11 of the Stamp Tax Regulations for land and housing leases and room tickets, and Item 13 for various cash receipts, 'If the amount is over 1 yuan but less than 10 yuan, a 1-cent stamp shall be affixed, and if the amount is over 10 yuan, a 2-cent stamp shall be affixed.' All must comply with the regulations and be affixed on each sheet. I am sincerely afraid that the landlords and sublessors do not understand the regulations, or there may be opportunistic evasion. The director of this bureau has now been ordered by the provincial bureau to supervise, assess, and strengthen the enforcement. It is my duty to rectify the levy. In addition to ordering the promoters to comply with it and sending personnel to inspect it at any time, it is hereby announced to the landlords and sublessors within the jurisdiction that they must all know that when using the above-mentioned rent books and sublease books, they must affix the stamps according to the regulations and do not evade them. Otherwise, once it is found out or reported, it will only be dealt with according to the law. Do not say that I did not warn you. Please comply with the order and do not violate it. Sincerely, this announcement. August 25, 21st year of the Republic of China, Director Xu Zhicheng."

Nanyang Bridge, French Concession

Repercussions of Demolishing Houses in Yufu Lane 146

House Tenants Gather to Discuss Coping Measures

The houses in Yufu Lane, Nanyang Bridge, French Concession, totaling over forty buildings, belong to the British-owned Hengye Real Estate Company. Recently, the company issued a notice to the tenants, stating that the houses would be demolished and rebuilt starting September 11th, and all tenants must vacate the premises. After receiving the notice, the tenants were all panicked, believing that the houses were not old and were quite sturdy, so there was no need for demolition. Therefore, they unanimously expressed their opposition and held a general meeting of all tenants at 3 p.m. yesterday at the Fourth District Branch of the Citizens' Federation. More than thirty people attended, and Yang Yingqi was elected as chairman. The following coping measures were decided: (1) The entire group will jointly send a letter to the landlord, stating the reasons and denying the need for reconstruction; (2) A delegation will be organized to be responsible for negotiations. Yang Yingqi, Ye Yuangen, Yang Youbin, Qin Guoliang, Tian Wenyong, Wang Ziting, Wang Laosan, and Xia Yongzhen were elected as representatives, with Yang Yingqi, Tian Wenyong, and Yang Youbin as the chief representatives to handle all matters; (3) Submit petitions to various agencies and organizations, requesting assistance; (4) Notify tenants not to act freely before a solution is reached, otherwise they will be regarded as public enemies; (5) Organize a registration form for reference; (6) If necessary, hire legal counsel to provide legal protection; (7) All public expenses will be shared by the entire group. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Shu Yuanhe's Injury Worsens 147

Sent to Hospital for Treatment

Fourth District of the City Federation Submits a Document

Regarding the case of Shu Yuanhe, the owner of Yiqingyong Wine Shop at No. 76 Milu Road, Nanyang Bridge, French Concession, being brutally beaten and injured by police officer No. 1154, the Shanghai Local Court Procuratorate has already verified the injuries and is awaiting orders to summon the offending police officer for interrogation. However, after Shu Yuanhe returned home, his injuries suddenly worsened yesterday, with persistent fever and extreme danger. His family has notified the lawyer handling the case and has also sent Shu to the hospital for treatment.

The Fourth District Branch of the Shanghai Second Special District Citizens' Federation of Nanyang Bridge, French Concession, submitted a petition to the Shanghai Municipal Government (the beginning is omitted): The letter from Yiqingyong Wine Shop, a member store of the association located at No. 76 Milu Road, French Concession, states that at approximately 4 a.m. on the 24th of this month, a cart loaded with liquor was being transported to Zhongshan Road in West Shanghai. Just as it left the shop and passed the police亭 near the Nanyang Bridge in the Chinese territory, police officer No. 1154 suddenly appeared to inspect the tax stamps and demanded four yuan. The shop manager immediately stated to the officer that the tax system had been changed to a special consolidated tax and no further tax stamps were needed. However, the officer ignored this and took both the goods and the shop manager to the Second District Headquarters for questioning. Subsequently, after reporting to the trade association and requesting the Consolidated Tax Bureau to provide confirmation from the Second District via telephone, the manager was released at approximately 11 a.m. Unexpectedly, less than half an hour later, officer No. 1154 returned to the shop and demanded a reward of four yuan from the manager, otherwise the goods would not be released. The shop believed that the officer's actions were illegal and refused to pay. Because the officer's demands were not met, he attempted to arrest the manager. Immediately afterward, a large number of plainclothes police officers, numbering seven or eight, arrived and destroyed seven jars of Shaoxing wine in the shop. They dragged the shop manager, Shu Yuanhe, away, beating him along the way with gun butts and fists. After arriving at the Second District Headquarters, they immediately put him in shackles and imprisoned him, without sending him to a hospital. Eventually, the French Concession police sent personnel to negotiate, and the shop manager was released, but he was already severely injured all over his body. The shop believes that police officers are meant to protect merchants and maintain local peace and tranquility. However, this officer not only failed to fulfill his duty but also acted lawlessly. The merchants and residents cannot tolerate this. Therefore, the shop specifically requests the association to promptly initiate negotiations to achieve the goal of punishing the perpetrators and obtaining compensation. Based on this information, the association immediately convened a temporary emergency meeting for discussion. It was unanimously agreed that the police officer was incompetent and ignorant of the law. Since the Consolidated Tax Bureau had already provided confirmation, how could he blindly demand payment and dare to brutally beat merchants, disrupting commerce? This type of action is extremely illegal. If he is not severely punished according to the law, how can the police administration be rectified and the laws be upheld? It was decided to submit a petition to the director, requesting him to order an investigation of the offending police officer and to severely punish him according to the law, in order to appease public anger and ensure local peace and stability. Therefore, a truthful petition is submitted, and it is requested that the director review it, and favorably handle the matter, for the benefit of the public, etc.

Zhang Longbi's Son

Zhang Xingruo Accused of Encroachment on Property 152

丨Transferred to the Civil Court for Trial丨

Yao Renjie, a local resident, 23 years old, learned the business of money shops from a young age and later switched to the plumbing industry. He lives at No. 22, Yinxiantang Lane, Vulcan Temple, Nanshi. His birth mother, Ms. Lu, passed away in 1924. At that time, the Jiangsu-Zhejiang War between Lu and Qi broke out, and the Nanshi area was unstable. In addition, Yao was only 14 years old and had not yet reached adulthood. Therefore, Ms. Lu, on her deathbed, entrusted all property deeds and evidence to her uncle, Zhang Xingruo (the son of the late famous doctor Zhang Longbi), for safekeeping. Now that Yao has reached adulthood, he wants to reclaim the property rights from Zhang. Unexpectedly, Zhang suddenly refused with excuses. Negotiations have continued to this day without any progress. Yao had no choice but to hire three lawyers, Zhao Zuwei, Lu Dingming, and Liu Weilun, to file a criminal self-accusation of encroachment with the First Special District Court against Zhang Xingruo, and to attach a civil lawsuit, demanding the return of the property evidence. On the 16th of this month, the First Special District Local Court held a hearing in the Fifth Criminal Chamber, presided over by Judge Huang Risheng. The defendant, Zhang Xingruo, did not appear. The court ordered a postponement of one week and instructed the plaintiff to accompany the Chinese police officer No. 2677 of the Hongkou Police Station to Zhang's residence at No. 146 Aiwenyi Road at 2 p.m. on the 21st to summon Zhang. On the 23rd of this month, the hearing was held again. The plaintiff, Yao Renjie, and the defendant, Zhang Xingruo (61 years old, from Shanghai), and the plaintiff's aunt, Zhang Yao (the wife of the defendant, Zhang Xingruo, 61 years old, from Shanghai), arrived at the court with their lawyers. Judge Huang continued the inquiry. However, the defendant denied that the plaintiff's mother had entrusted any receipts or evidence to him for safekeeping. He only admitted that the plaintiff's mother had deposited the property evidence with his wife, Zhang Yao, and that he had no knowledge of it. Zhang Yao also claimed that all the evidence had been entrusted to her by her brother (the plaintiff's deceased father) when he was dying in 1912. She also claimed that she was also entitled to a portion of the property in her own right. Judge Huang then instructed the lawyers of both parties to begin their arguments and declared the trial closed, ruling that the case was a dispute over property rights and ordering it to be transferred to the Civil Court for trial. Yao has now been instructed to continue the lawsuit in the Civil Court.
